Zina Under Coercion: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Hadd
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of coercion on hadd for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on whether coercion (ikrah) removes hadd for zina, distinguishing between coercion by the sultan and by others, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Coercion by the sultan always removes hadd; for others, the later fatwa is that hadd is also removed.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: does coercion (ikrah) exempt a person from the hadd punishment for zina? All agree that coercion by the sultan nullifies the hadd. But when the coercer is a non-sultan, Abu Hanifa initially held that hadd applies, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, maintained that the hadd is dropped. The text explains the reasoning behind each view and concludes that the fatwa today follows the companions' opinion due to changing times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Break down the cases: (1) coercion by the sultan → no hadd by consensus; (2) coercion by a non-sultan according to Abu Hanifa → hadd applies; (3) coercion by a non-sultan according to the two companions → no hadd.
Note that Zufar and an early view of Abu Hanifa also held that hadd applies even for sultan coercion, but that view was abandoned.
2
Analyze the reasoning for sultan's case
Why does coercion by the sultan remove hadd? The text implies because ikrah (fear of death/harm) nullifies consent. Even though an erection might suggest willingness, the possibility of natural erection (as in sleep) creates a doubt that averts hadd.
This uses the Hanafi principle that hadd is averted by doubts (al-hadd yudra'u bi al-shubuhat).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute for non-sultan coercion
Understand the effective cause (illa): Abu Hanifa limits valid ikrah to the sultan because non-sultan coercion can be resisted or help sought from the sultan. The companions extend it to any overpowering person because the real factor is fear of destruction (khawf al-halak), which exists regardless of the coercer's identity.
This disagreement is fundamentally about the definition of effective duress.
4
Recognize the historical contingency
The text mentions 'ikhtilaf 'asr' — the difference is due to changing times. In Abu Hanifa's era, no private individual had enough power to be irresistible. By the time of the companions, tyrants and strongmen existed, making duress from non-sultans credible.
This shows that fatwa can shift with social realities while remaining within the school's methodology.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
The text states 'yufta bi qawlihima' — fatwa is given by the companions' view. This is the mufta bihi position because it better addresses contemporary conditions. Authority_weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa).
In fatwa practice, the opinion that is more precautionary or more suited to the times is often given precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبإكراه أي من أكرهه السلطان على الزنا فزنى فلا حد عليه، وقال زفر يحد، وهو قول أبي حنيفة أولاً؛ لأن الزنا من الرجل لا يكون إلا بعد انتشار الآلة، وانتشار الآلة آية الطوع ولنا أن الانتشار قد يكون طبعاً كما في النائم فأورث شبهة، وإن أكره غير السلطان حد عنده وقالا لا يحد، وهذا بناء على أن الإكراه لا يتحقق إلا السلطان عنده؛ لأن إكراه غيره لا يدوم؛ ولأنه يمكن الاستغاثة بالسلطان في إكراه غيره، وعندهما: يتحقق الإكراه من كل متغلب؛ لأن المؤثر خوف الهلاك، وهو يتحقق من غير السلطان أيضاً، وقيل: هذا اختلاف عصر، ففي زمنه لم يكن تغيره من القوة ما لم يمكن دفعه، وكانت في زمنهما لكل متغلب فيفتى بقولهما. (مستخلص، فتح)
And [the section on] coercion: i.e., whoever is coerced by the sultan to commit zina and does so, there is no hadd on him. Zufar said he is stoned, and it was Abu Hanifa's first opinion; because zina from a man only occurs after the emergence of the organ, and the emergence of the organ is a sign of willingness. But we [say] that emergence may be natural, as in a sleeper, so it creates a doubt. And if the coercer is other than the sultan, Abu Hanifa [later] said he is stoned, while the two companions said he is not stoned. This is based on the fact that coercion is only realized from the sultan according to him [Abu Hanifa], because coercion by others does not persist, and because one can seek help from the sultan against coercion by others. According to them [the two companions], coercion is realized from any overpowering person, because the effective factor is fear of destruction, and that is also realized from non-sultan figures. It is said that this is a difference of time: in Abu Hanifa's time, there was no one of such strength that he could not be repelled, but in the time of the two companions, every tyrant had such power, so fatwa is given by their view. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses zina committed under coercion (ikrah). If the sultan (ruler) coerces a man into committing zina, there is no hadd on the man by agreement. Zufar (a Hanafi) and earlier Abu Hanifa held that hadd applies because an erection indicates willingness, but the later Hanafi position is that even natural erection (as in sleep) can occur without true consent, so there is a doubt. For coercion by non-sultan, Abu Hanifa's final view is that hadd applies, while the two companions say it does not, because they recognize coercion from any overpowering person if there is genuine fear of death. The text concludes that this disagreement may be due to changing historical circumstances: in Abu Hanifa's time, no private individual could be so overpowering, so coercion by non-sultan was not considered effective; but in the time of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, tyrants existed, so fatwa is given by their opinion (i.e., no hadd).

Key Terms
الإكراه (al-ikrah): Coercion, specifically duress that nullifies consent and can eliminate hadd for zina.
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or governmental authority, whose coercion is considered lasting and irresistible in the Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi position (two companions), if a man is forced by a powerful civilian to commit zina, what is the ruling?
A) The hadd is still applied
B) The hadd is not applied
C) Only the coercer is punished
D) The man must pay compensation

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that coercion by any overwhelming force removes the hadd for zina, due to the doubt it creates and changing circumstances.

Hadd with Partial Confession and Denial of One Party
Ruling on hadd when only one of the two confesses and the other denies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd when only one party confesses to zina and the other denies, and distinguish between the two scenarios (claim of marriage vs. complete denial).

Core Idea
A single party's confession does not enforce hadd if the other denies or claims shubha.

In Hanafi law, hadd for zina requires either four witnesses or multiple confessions from the confessor. But what happens when only one party confesses and the other denies? This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies two scenarios and their consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the confession requirement
Note that the confessor must confess four times for hadd to be considered. Here, the confessor does confess four times, but the other party denies.
Confession is one of the means to establish zina, but it alone is not sufficient if the other party contradicts.
2
Distinguish scenario one: claim of marriage
If the confessor says 'I committed zina' but the other says 'We were married', the claim of marriage creates a shubha (doubt) that prevents hadd. The confessor is not stoned but must pay the dower (mahr).
A claim of marriage, even if not proven, is enough to create doubt sufficient to block hadd.
3
Distinguish scenario two: complete denial
If the confessor says 'I committed zina with X' and X says 'I don't know him' or 'It didn't happen', then the hadd is also not enforced. The confession alone is insufficient without corroboration.
In this case, no shubha is claimed; the denial alone blocks hadd.
4
Note the financial consequence
In scenario one, the confessor must pay the mahr (dower) because the intercourse is deemed to have occurred under a shubha. In scenario two, the text does not mention any financial obligation; presumably, no mahr is due because the denial is total.
The 'aqr (dower) is equivalent to the mahr of women of similar status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبإقرار: أي ولا يجب أيضاً بإقرار أحد الزانيين. (عيني) إن أنكره الآخر هذه المسألة على وجهين: أحدهما: أن يقر الرجل أربعاً بالزنا بفلانة، وقالت المرأة: إنه تزوجني أو أقرت المرأة بالزنا أربعاً مع فلان، وقال فلان تزوجتها لم يحد، ويجب العقر، وإن كانت معترفة بأن لا مهر لها، وثانيهما أن يقر أربعاً أنه زنى بفلانة، فقالت: ما زنى بي ولا أعرفه أو أقرت هي أربعاً بالزنا مع فلان، وقال فلان ما زينت بها، ولا أعرفها، فلا يحد عند حنيفة، والحاصل أن في الوجه الأول وهو ما إذا أقر أحدهما وأنكر الآخر وادعى شبهة هي التزوج لا يحد
And [the section on] confession: i.e., it is not obligatory also by the confession of one of the two [adulterers]. (Ayni) If the other denies it. This issue has two aspects: First: if a man confesses four times to zina with a certain woman, and the woman says 'He married me', or if the woman confesses four times to zina with a certain man, and the man says 'I married her', then the confessor is not stoned, and the dower (mahr) is obligatory, even if she admits that she has no mahr. Second: if he confesses four times that he committed zina with a certain woman, and she says 'He did not commit zina with me and I do not know him', or she confesses four times to zina with a certain man, and he says 'I did not commit zina with her and I do not know her', then he is not stoned according to Hanifa. The conclusion in the first case is that if one confesses and the other denies and claims a doubt (shubha) which is marriage, the confessor is not stoned.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of confession (iqrar) in zina cases when only one party confesses and the other denies. There are two scenarios. First, if the man confesses to zina with a woman, but the woman claims they were married (creating a shubha), the man is not given hadd (since his confession alone is not enough without corroboration or multiple confessions? but here he confesses four times, yet the woman's claim of marriage creates doubt). Instead, he must pay the mahr (dower). Even if the woman admits she had no mahr, it is still paid. The second scenario is where one confesses and the other denies entirely (not even acknowledging being known). In that case, the confessor is also not stoned. The reasoning seems to be that a single party's confession is insufficient for hadd if the other does not confirm. The hadd requires either four witnesses or multiple confessions from both? Only the confessor's admission is not enough to impose hadd on either.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession; in zina, it must be made four times to lead to hadd.
العقر (al-'aqr): The mandatory dower (mahr) paid in case of intercourse under a void contract or shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man confesses four times to zina with a woman, but the woman says she was married to him, what is the ruling?
A) Both are stoned
B) Only the man is stoned
C) The man is not stoned but must pay mahr
D) The woman is stoned for lying

Key Takeaway
A confession to zina, even if repeated four times, does not lead to hadd if the other party denies or claims a shubha like marriage.

Zina with a Minor or Insane Person: The Woman's Liability
Ruling on zina by minor/insane and its effect on the woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for a woman who commits zina with a minor or insane person and explain the reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
A woman is not hadded for zina with a minor or insane because their act lacks legal address.

This lesson examines a specific dispute in Islamic criminal law: when a sane adult woman willingly engages in zina with a minor or an insane person, is she liable for hadd? The Hanafi school says no, while other schools say yes. Understanding the Hanafi reasoning will sharpen your grasp of how legal capacity (ahliyyah) affects criminal liability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that the woman is not subject to hadd, and note that the minor/insane partner is also not hadded by consensus.
The text explicitly says 'ولا تحد المرأة أيضاً عندنا' (the woman is also not hadded according to us).
2
Identify the opposing view
Zufar (within Hanafi) and the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that the woman must be hadded.
They argue that each person is accountable for their own act.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing dalil: 'because the lapse of hadd on the one who complied does not affect her right, because each of them is held accountable for his own action'.
This means the minor/insane's lack of liability does not erase the woman's own criminal act.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi proof: zina is the act of one who is legally addressed to abstain (mukhatab bil kaff). The minor/insane is not legally addressed, so his act is not zina in the full sense, and therefore the woman's act does not meet the condition for hadd.
The key concept: the nature of the act is defined by the capacity of the doer.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi fiqh, a woman who willingly commits zina with a minor or insane person escapes hadd, whereas in other schools she would be punished. Conversely, if a sane adult man commits zina with a minor or insane woman, he is hadded by consensus.
This asymmetry is a distinctive feature of Hanafi criminal law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزنا صبي إلخ: أي إذا زنا صبي أو مجنون بامرأة عاقلة بالغة فلا حد على الصبي والمجنون بالإجماع، ولا تحد المرأة أيضاً عندنا، وقال زفر والثلاثة: يجب عليها الحد؛ لأن امتناع الحد على المطاوع له لا يخل في حقها؛ لأن كلاً منهما مؤاخذ بفعله، ولنا: أن الزنا فعل من هو مخاطب بالكف، وفعل الصبي والمجنون ليس بهذه الصفة، فلا يكون موجباً للحد، وقوله: بخلاف عكسه" وهو ما إذا زنى العاقل البالغ بصبية أو مجنونة حيث يجب الحد على الرجل بالاتفاق. (مستخلص عيني بخلاف عكسه: أي لو زنى عاقل بالغ بمحبوبته أو صبية يجامع مثلها حد الرجل خاصة إجماعاً. (عيني)
And concerning zina of a boy or an insane person: meaning if a boy or an insane person commits zina with a sane adult woman, there is no hadd on the boy and the insane person by consensus, and the woman is also not subjected to hadd according to us. Zufar and the three said: hadd is obligatory upon her because the lapse of hadd on the one who complied does not affect her right, because each of them is held accountable for his own action. Our proof: zina is the act of one who is addressed to abstain, and the act of the boy and insane person is not of this description, so it does not necessitate hadd. His statement: contrary to its opposite – that is when a sane adult commits zina with a girl or an insane woman, where hadd is obligatory upon the man by agreement. (Extract from Ayni: contrary to its opposite: meaning if a sane adult commits zina with his beloved or a girl of cohabitable age, the man alone is hadded by consensus. (Ayni))
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute regarding the liability for hadd punishment when one party to zina is a minor or insane. The Hanafi position, as explained by the commentator, is that no hadd is imposed on the minor or insane person by consensus. Furthermore, the woman who willingly engages in zina with them is also not subject to hadd according to Abu Hanifa. The proof offered is that zina is defined as an act of one who is legally addressed to abstain (mukhatab bil kaff). Since minors and the insane are not legally addressed, their act does not constitute zina in the full legal sense, and thus does not trigger the hadd punishment for the woman. In contrast, if a sane adult man commits zina with a minor or insane female, he is subject to hadd by consensus, as he is legally addressed. The opposing view of Zufar and the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) holds that the woman should also be hadded because each person is responsible for their own action.

Key Terms
صبي (sabiyy): A male child who has not reached puberty.
مجنون (majnun): An insane person lacking legal address (mukhatab).
حد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes like zina.
مخاطب بالكف (mukhatab bil kaff): One who is legally addressed to abstain from an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a mature woman commits zina with an insane man, what is the ruling?
A) Both are stoned.
B) The woman is lashed.
C) Neither is punished.
D) Only the man is punished.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a woman is not subject to hadd if she commits zina with a minor or an insane person, because the partner's act lacks the legal character of zina.

Zina with a Hired Woman: The Hanafi Shubha Exception
Ruling on zina with a hired woman and the shubha argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for zina with a hired woman, explain the shubha argument from the Quran and the reported incident, and contrast it with the view of the Sahibayn and other schools.

Core Idea
Payment for sex as a stipulated condition creates a shubha akin to dower, averting the hadd—a uniquely Hanafi position.

This passage addresses a controversial corner of hadd law: does a man who pays for sexual intercourse thereby avoid the fixed punishment? The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa, answers yes, based on a creative analogy between the payment and a dower. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the intra- and inter-madhhab disagreements, clarifying the conditions under which the hadd is averted.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man hires a woman specifically for sexual intercourse and then has intercourse, the hadd is not obligatory. Identify the act and the ruling.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that hadd is obligatory because there is no ownership or semblance of ownership; it is pure zina. The three other imams concur.
The intra-Hanafi disagreement is between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing view argues that no shubha exists since no valid marriage contract or ownership is present; therefore, the act is plain zina requiring the full hadd.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's proof includes a reported incident where the Prophet dropped the hadd because the payment was considered her dower, and the Quranic verse (5:5) that calls the dower 'wages' (ujur). This creates a shubha that averts the hadd.
The analogy to a marriage contract for zina (which also averts hadd) supports the shubha.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi law (following Abu Hanifa), a man hiring a woman explicitly for sexual relations is not subject to hadd, whereas in other schools he is. The consensus case is when payment is given without stipulation—then hadd applies.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, though some later authorities consider the case mixed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالزنا بمستأجرة: أي إذا استأجر امرأة ليزني بها فوطئها لا يجب الحد عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: يجب الحد؛ لأن ليس بينهما ملك ولا شبهة ملك، فكان زناً محضاً ، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله ما روي أن امرأة طلبت من رجل مالا فأبى أن يعطيها . تمكنه حتى ه الحد عنهما، وقال: "هذا مهرها ، ولأنه تعالى سمى المهر أجرة نفسها، فدراً عمر من بقوله تعالى: إِذَا آتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ (المائدة:٥)، فصارت شبهة، ولهذا لو قال: أمهرتك كذا لأزني بك لم يجب الحد فكذا إذا قال: استأجرتك أو خذي هذا لأطأك أو مكنيني نفسك بكذا. رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٤/١] ولو استأجرها للخدمة فزنى بها يجب الحد بلا خلاف، والحاصل أن الخلاف فيما إذا أعطاها مالاً واشترط التمكين، أما إذا أعطاها مالاً ولم يشترط ثم جامعها يحد إجماعاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
And concerning zina with a hired woman: meaning if a man hires a woman to commit zina with her and he has intercourse, the hadd is not obligatory according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is obligatory because there is neither ownership nor semblance of ownership between them, so it is pure zina, and the three held this view. His proof: it is related that a woman asked a man for money and he refused to give it to her until she enabled him [to have intercourse], and he dropped the hadd from both and said: 'This is her dower.' And because Allah Almighty called the dower 'wages' (ujur) in the verse: 'When you give them their wages' (Quran 5:5), so a semblance (shubha) arises. For this reason, if he said: 'I dower you with such-and-such for zina with you,' hadd is not obligatory, similarly if he said: 'I hire you' or 'Take this so I can have intercourse with you' or 'Allow me for such-and-such.' (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/384) And if he hired her for service and then committed zina with her, hadd is obligatory without disagreement. The gist is that the disagreement is when he gives her money and stipulates allowance. But if he gives her money without stipulating and then has intercourse, he is hadded by consensus. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of hiring a woman for the purpose of zina. According to Abu Hanifa, no hadd is imposed because the payment creates a semblance (shubha) of dower, which averts the hadd. The proof includes a reported incident where a woman demanded payment for intercourse and the man was excused, and a Quranic verse calling the dower 'wages'. Thus, the payment is analogous to dower. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold that hadd is obligatory because there is no ownership or semblance, so it is pure zina. The three other imams agree with them. The practical distinction: if the payment is expressly for the sexual act, it creates a shubha; if the hiring is for service and then zina occurs, hadd is imposed by consensus.

Key Terms
مستأجرة (musta'jara): A woman hired specifically for the purpose of sexual intercourse.
شبهة (shubha): A semblance or doubt that nullifies the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for averting the hadd punishment in the case of zina with a hired woman according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The woman's consent.
B) The payment being stipulated as a condition analogous to dower.
C) The man being unmarried.
D) Both parties being unmarried.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts a man from hadd for zina with a hired woman if the payment is stipulated as a condition, due to shubha, but the act remains sinful and subject to ta'zir.

Zina Under Coercion: Ruler vs Non-Ruler Coercion
Ruling on zina under coercion – intra-Hanafi dispute on ruler vs non-ruler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zina under coercion by the ruler vs others, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Coercion by the ruler averts hadd for zina; for other coercers, the later fatwa follows Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that no hadd applies.

The hadd punishment for zina is severe, but what if the act is committed under coercion? Hanafi jurists distinguish between coercion by the ruler and by others. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the intra-Hanafi dispute and the final position adopted for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) committed under coercion. The general ruling is that hadd is averted when coercion is by the ruler. For non-ruler coercion, there was disagreement.
Coercion creates a shubha (doubt) that blocks hadd.
2
Analyze the dispute over ruler coercion
All Hanafi authorities agree: if the ruler coerces, no hadd. Zufar disagreed, but the Hanafi response is that erection can occur naturally (as in sleep), so it does not prove willingness.
The ruler's coercion is considered overwhelming and lasting.
3
Analyze the dispute over non-ruler coercion
Abu Hanifa initially held hadd is imposed because coercion from non-rulers is not lasting and one can seek help from the ruler. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that any powerful person (mutaghallib) can coerce effectively, as fear of destruction is the same.
This led to a difference in fatwa.
4
Apply the tarjih and identify the mufta bihi
Over time, non-ruler coercion became irresistible, so the companions' view is adopted for fatwa. The mufta bihi is: no hadd for coercion from any powerful person.
The text states 'فيفتى بقولهما' (fatwa is given according to their view).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبإكراه أي من أكرهه السلطان على الزنا فزنى فلا حد عليه، وقال زفر يحد، وهو قول أبي حنيفة أولاً؛ لأن الزنا من الرجل لا يكون إلا بعد انتشار الآلة، وانتشار الآلة آية الطوع ولنا أن الانتشار قد يكون طبعاً كما في النائم فأورث شبهة، وإن أكره غير السلطان حد عنده وقالا لا يحد، وهذا بناء على أن الإكراه لا يتحقق إلا السلطان عنده؛ لأن إكراه غيره لا يدوم؛ ولأنه يمكن الاستغاثة بالسلطان في إكراه غيره، وعندهما: يتحقق الإكراه من كل متغلب؛ لأن المؤثر خوف الهلاك، وهو يتحقق من غير السلطان أيضاً، وقيل: هذا اختلاف عصر، ففي زمنه لم يكن تغيره من القوة ما لم يمكن دفعه، وكانت في زمنهما لكل متغلب فيفتى بقولهما. (مستخلص، فتح)
And concerning coercion: meaning whoever is coerced by the ruler to commit zina and does so, there is no hadd upon him. Zufar said he is hadded, and that was Abu Hanifa's earlier view. Because zina from a man only occurs after erection, and erection is a sign of willingness. Our proof: erection may occur naturally as in sleep, so it creates a shubha. If the coercion is from other than the ruler, he is hadded according to Abu Hanifa, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no hadd. This is based on the fact that coercion is only realized from the ruler according to Abu Hanifa, because coercion from others is not lasting, and one can seek aid from the ruler. According to the two, coercion is realized from anyone with power, because the effect is fear of destruction, and that exists from others as well. It is said this is a difference of era: in his time, usurpers were not strong enough to be irresistible, but in their time, there were powerful usurpers, so the fatwa is given according to their view. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of coercion on the hadd punishment for zina. The ruling depends on who coerces. If the ruler (political authority) coerces a man to commit zina, no hadd is imposed according to the later Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa's final view and the two companions). Zufar held that hadd is still obligatory because erection indicates willingness, but the Hanafis respond that erection can occur naturally (as in sleep), so it does not exclude coercion. If the coercion is from someone other than the ruler, Abu Hanifa initially said hadd is obligatory, but the two companions said no hadd. Their reasoning: true coercion requires a threat of destruction that cannot be avoided, and that can come from any powerful person (mutaghallib), not only the ruler. Some scholars attribute this difference to changing times: in Abu Hanifa's era, non-ruler coercion was not irresistible, but later it was, so the fatwa is given according to the companions' view.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Compulsion by threat of harm that overcomes will.
سلطان (sultan): The political ruler who has authority to coerce.
متغلب (mutaghallib): A person who has seized power or is overwhelmingly strong.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that averts the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi position, if a man is forced to commit zina by a ruler, what is the ruling?
A) He is subject to hadd.
B) No hadd is imposed.
C) He receives a discretionary punishment.
D) The ruler is punished instead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately rules that coercion—whether by ruler or any powerful person—averts the hadd punishment for zina due to shubha.

Zina Confession by One Party: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Hadd
Ruling when one party confesses and the other denies zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two scenarios of unilateral confession in zina and explain why Abu Hanifa differs from the two companions regarding the application of hadd.

Core Idea
A unilateral confession of zina does not lead to hadd when the other party claims marriage; if simply denied, dispute arises.

This passage from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq explores a nuanced scenario: when one party confesses to zina and the other denies. It presents two distinct subcases, one where the denial is accompanied by a claim of marriage (shubha), another where it is a bare denial. The ruling differs in each, and within the second scenario, a well-known intra-Hanafi disagreement surfaces between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two aspects described: (1) the confessor claims zina, the other claims marriage; (2) the confessor claims zina, the other simply denies without any claim.
2
Analyze the agreed ruling in the first scenario
In the first scenario, both parties are immune from hadd by consensus, and the woman receives the dower (ajr) even if she admits no dower. Understand the reasoning: the claim of marriage creates a shubha that blocks hadd.
Shubha is a key concept in Hanafi hudud law.
3
Examine the disputed ruling in the second scenario
In the second scenario, the denier is never hadded by consensus, but there is a dispute regarding the confessor: Abu Hanifa says no hadd; the two companions say the confessor is hadded.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Grasp the reasoning of the two companions
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that a confession is binding on oneself, and the denier's bare denial does not negate the confessor's admission. Therefore, the confessor should be punished.
They give weight to the confessor's own words.
5
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that the bare denial creates doubt (shubha) because the other party could be telling the truth, and hadd is repelled by doubts. The confession alone is not enough to overcome this doubt.
The principle: 'Hadd is avoided in cases of doubt.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبإقرار: أي ولا يجب أيضاً بإقرار أحد الزانيين. (عيني) إن أنكره الآخر هذه المسألة على وجهين: أحدهما: أن يقر الرجل أربعاً بالزنا بفلانة، وقالت المرأة: إنه تزوجني أو أقرت المرأة بالزنا أربعاً مع فلان، وقال فلان تزوجتها لم يحد، ويجب العقر، وإن كانت معترفة بأن لا مهر لها، وثانيهما أن يقر أربعاً أنه زنى بفلانة، فقالت: ما زنى بي ولا أعرفه أو أقرت هي أربعاً بالزنا مع فلان، وقال فلان ما زينت بها، ولا أعرفها، فلا يحد عند حنيفة، والحاصل أن في الوجه الأول وهو ما إذا أقر أحدهما وأنكر الآخر وادعى شبهة هي التزوج لا يحد واحد منهما بالاتفاق، وفي الوجه الثاني وهو ما إذا أقر أحدهما وأنكر الآخر ولم يدع شبهة، لا يحد المنكر بالاتفاق، ويحد المقر عندهما لا عنده. (فتح)
And concerning confession: meaning it is also not obligatory due to the confession of one of the two adulterers. (Ayni) If the other denies it: this issue has two aspects: One: that the man confesses four times to zina with a certain woman, and she says: 'He married me,' or the woman confesses four times to zina with a certain man, and he says: 'I married her,' then neither is hadded, and the bridal gift (ajr) is obligatory, even if she admits she has no dower. The second aspect: that he confesses four times that he committed zina with a certain woman, and she says: 'He did not commit zina with me and I do not know him,' or she confesses four times to zina with a certain man, and he says: 'I have not committed zina with her and I do not know her,' then according to Hanifa (Abu Hanifa) neither is hadded. The summary is that in the first aspect, when one confesses and the other denies and claims a shubha (marriage), neither is hadded by agreement. In the second aspect, when one confesses and the other denies and does not claim a shubha, the denier is not hadded by agreement, and the confessor is hadded according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) but not according to Abu Hanifa. (Fath)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage details the effect of a confession of zina by one party while the other denies. Two scenarios are discussed. First, if the confessor says 'I committed zina with so-and-so' and the other says 'He/she married me,' claiming a shubha (marriage), then no hadd is imposed on either by consensus. The woman is entitled to the dower (ajr) even if she admits she has no dower. Second, if the other party simply denies any knowledge or involvement (no claim of shubha), then there is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa says no hadd is imposed on the confessor either, while his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the confessor is subject to hadd. The denier is never hadded by agreement. The underlying principle is that a confession of zina against oneself is not fully effective when the other party denies, because hadd cannot be established solely by confession if there is a possibility of false confession or shubha.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession of having committed zina, typically required four times.
عقر (ajr/uqr): The bridal gift (dower) owed to a woman in case of marriage or as compensation in cases of shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario (where one confesses and the other claims marriage), what is the agreed ruling according to all Hanafi scholars?
A) Both are hadded.
B) The confessor is hadded, the other is not.
C) Neither is hadded, and the woman receives the dower.
D) The denier is hadded for false accusation.

Key Takeaway
A unilateral confession of zina leads to hadd only when the other party does not assert a shubha and even then the confessor's hadd is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his companions.

Zina with a Slave-Girl and Killing: Hadd or Not?
Ruling on committing zina with a slave-girl and then killing her

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the punishment for a man who commits zina with a slave-girl and then kills her, and explain the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and the rebuttal of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Killing a slave-girl after zina prevents ownership from averting hadd, so both punishments apply.

This lesson examines a case where a man commits zina with a slave-girl and then kills her. The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Yusuf argues that the liability for the value creates a semblance of ownership that bars the hadd, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that killing destroys the subject of ownership, so both hadd and value are due. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists apply the principle of shubha in hudud.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: both hadd for zina and payment of the slave-girl's value are obligatory.
This is the majority view within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds that only the value is due; the hadd is averted because the liability for value implies a form of ownership that creates a shubha.
Abu Yusuf is the prominent dissenter here.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf analogizes to a thief who steals an item and then becomes its owner before the hand is amputated: ownership nullifies the hadd. Here, paying the value is like acquiring ownership, so hadd should fall.
He also cites the case of zina causing loss of eyesight, where ownership over the blind body creates a shubha and averts hadd.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad differentiate: in the killing case, the slave-girl no longer exists, so true ownership cannot be established. The liability is for destroying property, not for acquisition. The loss-of-eyesight case is different because the body remains, so ownership can be established.
Thus the analogy fails.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the majority view, the man is punished with hadd and must pay value; under Abu Yusuf, only value is due. The majority view is the mufta bihi.
All agree that if he first usurped, then committed zina, then paid value, no hadd (consensus).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن زنى بأمة فقتلها لزمه الحد والقيمة، وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يحد؛ لأن تقرر ضمان القيمة بسبب تملك الأمة فصار كما إذا اشتراها بعد ما زنى بها واعتراض سبب الملك قبل إقامة الحد يوجب سقوط الحد كما إذا ملك المسروق قبل القطع يسقط عنه القطع، ولهما: أنه ضمان قتل فلا يوجب الملك؛ لأن محل الملك قد فات، بخلاف ما إذا زنى بها فأذهب عينها بالزنا حيث يجب عليه قيمتها ويسقط الحد؛ لأن الملك قد ثبت في الجثة العمياء، فأورث الشبهة الدارئة للحد، ولو غصبها ثم زنى بها ثم ضمن قيمتها فلا حد عليه عندهم جميعاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
And whoever commits zina with a slave-girl and then kills her, both hadd and the price (value) are obligatory upon him. From Abu Yusuf: he is not hadded because the establishment of liability for the value due to taking ownership of the slave-girl, so it becomes as if he bought her after having committed zina with her, and the intervention of a cause of ownership before the enforcement of hadd causes the lapse of hadd, just as if he takes ownership of a stolen item before amputation, it nullifies the amputation. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it is a liability for killing, which does not establish ownership because the subject of ownership has perished, unlike the case where he commits zina with her and destroys her eyesight in the act, where he must pay her value and the hadd is waived because ownership is established in the blind body (juththa 'amya'), thus creating a shubha that averts hadd. And if he usurps her, then commits zina, then pays her value, there is no hadd upon him by consensus. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a man who commits zina with a slave-girl and then kills her. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he is subject to both the hadd punishment for zina and must pay the market value of the slave-girl to her owner. Abu Yusuf holds that he is only liable for the value, not the hadd, because the obligation of paying the value arises from taking ownership (tamalluk) of the slave-girl through the liability, and ownership before the hadd is enforced nullifies the hadd, analogous to a thief who owns the stolen item before amputation of the hand. The response of the two is that this is a liability for killing, not for taking ownership, because the subject of ownership (the slave-girl) no longer exists. They distinguish from the case where zina alone causes loss of eyesight: there, the slave-girl still exists (though blind), so ownership can be established, creating a shubha that averts hadd. In the case of killing, the body is destroyed, so no ownership can arise. All agree that if he usurps her first, then commits zina, then pays her value, no hadd is imposed.

Key Terms
قيمة (qima): The market value of the slave-girl to be paid as compensation.
شبهة دارئة (shubha dari'a): A semblance that averts (deflects) the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the punishment for a man who commits zina with a slave-girl and then kills her?
A) Only hadd for zina.
B) Only payment of her value.
C) Both hadd and payment of her value.
D) No punishment because of shubha.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, killing a slave-girl after zina does not create a shubha that averts hadd because the subject of ownership no longer exists.

Why the Caliph Is Not Subject to Hadd but Is Liable for Qisas and Financial Claims
Ruler's liability for crimes: subject to qisas and financial penalties but not hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the caliph's liability for hudud, qisas, and financial claims, and state the rational proof (dalil aqli) for the exemption from hadd.

Core Idea
The ruler is exempt from hadd because he enforces it; he cannot punish himself, but he must pay for private wrongs.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi principle regarding the head of state's criminal liability. The caliph is not above the law—he is liable for qisas and damages—but he is not subject to hadd punishments for crimes like zina, qadhf, or drinking. The reasoning is rooted in the nature of huquq Allah versus huquq al-ibad and the practical impossibility of self-enforcement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the ruling on the caliph? He is subject to qisas and financial claims but not to hadd punishments.
Hadd includes fixed penalties for zina, qadhf, shurb al-khamr, and theft.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a rational argument: the caliph is the enforcer of hadd, cannot enforce it on himself, and his deputy's act is like his own.
The source states: 'because hadd is a right of Allah and he is tasked with its enforcement, so he cannot enforce it on himself.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key point: hadd is designed for deterrence through public humiliation by an authority. The caliph cannot do that to himself, and no one else can because he has no superior.
The text says: 'deterrence is achieved by the enforcement of another, not by one's own act.'
4
Note the scope of the exemption
The exemption applies only to hadd (huquq Allah). For huquq al-ibad (qisas, financial claims), the caliph is fully liable.
The source explicitly says 'he is taken to account for financial matters.'
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
The caliph's exemption from hadd does not mean impunity. He remains accountable for private wrongs, and the community may enforce qisas or compel payment.
This balances the ruler's authority with justice for individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخليفة يؤخذ بالقصاص وبالأموال لا بالحد: أي لا يؤخذ الخليفة بالحدود، والخليفة الإمام الذي ليس فوقه إمام فإذا قذف إنساناً أو شرب حمراً أو زنى لا يحد؛ لأن الحدود حق الله تعالى، وهو المكلف بإقامتها، فلا يقدر على إقامتها على نفسه؛ لأن فائدة الإقامة الزجر والزجر بإقامة الغير لا بفعل نفسه؛ إذ الإقامة بطريق الخزي والنكال ولا يفعل ذلك أحد بنفسه وفعل نائبه كفعله؛ لأنه بأمره، فإذا لم يقدر لم يشرع. (مستخلص) وبالأموال: أي وكذا يؤخذ بالأموال إذا أتلف مال إنسان بغير حق فإنها من حقوق العباد أيضاً فيستوفي من ماله.
And the caliph (ruler) is subject to qisas (retaliation) and to financial claims, but not to hadd: meaning the caliph is not subjected to hadd punishments. The caliph is the Imam who has no Imam above him. So if he slanders someone, drinks wine, or commits zina, he is not hadded, because hadd punishments are the right of Allah, and he is the one tasked with enforcing them, so he cannot enforce them upon himself, because the benefit of enforcement is deterrence, and deterrence is achieved by the enforcement of another, not by one's own act; since enforcement is by way of humiliation and punishment, and no one does that to himself. The act of his deputy is like his own act because it is by his command. So since he cannot do it, it is not legislated. (Mukhtasar) And concerning financial claims: meaning he is also taken to account for financial matters: if he destroys someone's property without right, he must pay from his own wealth, because these are rights of the people (huquq al-ibad).
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage establishes a special principle regarding the head of state (caliph or imam) and punishment. The caliph is subject to qisas (retaliation for homicide or injury) and must pay for any financial damage he causes, but he is not subject to hadd punishments for crimes like slander (qadhf), drinking wine, or zina. The rationale is that hadd punishments are the rights of Allah (huquq Allah), and the caliph is the authority responsible for enforcing them. He cannot enforce them on himself because the purpose of hadd is deterrence through public humiliation and punishment by another. Since he has no superior, and his deputy acts on his behalf (which is like his own action), no one can carry out the hadd on him. Therefore, the hadd is not prescribed for him. However, rights of people (huquq al-ibad) such as qisas and financial compensation are enforceable because they are the claims of individuals, and the caliph can be held accountable by the injured party or their representatives, possibly with the help of the Muslim community.

Key Terms
خليفة (khalifa): The supreme political leader (imam) with no one above him.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments for crimes like zina, qadhf, shurb al-khamr.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation for homicide or injury, a right of the victim.
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights that belong to Allah, such as hadd punishments.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): Rights of individuals, such as qisas and financial claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the caliph is above the law.
B) Because hadd is a right of Allah and the caliph is the enforcer; he cannot enforce it on himself.
C) Because the caliph always repents before enforcement.
D) Because hadd is only for commoners.

Key Takeaway
The caliph is exempt from hadd because he cannot enforce it on himself, but he remains fully liable for qisas and financial claims, reflecting the Hanafi distinction between huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad.

Zina with Killing of a Slave Woman: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Hadd and Shubha
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shubha from guarantee of value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf on whether hadd is imposed when a man kills the slave woman he committed zina with, and apply the concept of shubha to analyse the dispute.

Core Idea
Guarantee for killing does not create ownership, so hadd is not dropped.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement. The central question: if a man commits zina with a slave woman and kills her during the act, does he face both hadd and financial compensation, or does the financial guarantee create a shubha that drops the hadd? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad maintain that both penalties are due, while Abu Yusuf argues that the guarantee of value creates ownership, forming a shubha that repels the hadd. Understanding this dispute sharpens our grasp of how the Hanafi school applies shubha in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The base text (matn) states: 'Whoever commits zina with a slave woman and kills her, upon him is the hadd and the value.' This is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Recognize the disagreement
Abu Yusuf opposes: he holds no hadd because the guarantee of value creates ownership, which forms a shubha. Understand his reasoning.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf) vs Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's analogy
Abu Yusuf analogizes to the case where a man buys the slave woman after zina. In that case, ownership drops the hadd. He argues that the guarantee of value similarly creates ownership. Also analogized to theft: if thief owns stolen property before amputation, amputation is dropped.
4
Understand the counter-argument
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond: the guarantee is for killing, not for zina. The slave is dead, so ownership cannot arise because the subject of ownership has perished. Therefore, no shubha. This distinguishes it from the case where the slave is alive after zina, where ownership does arise and hadd is dropped.
5
Note the agreed exception
If the slave was obtained by force (ghasb) before zina and then killed, all agree hadd is dropped. This shows that when ownership is genuinely established, it creates a shubha. The guarantee for killing does not establish ownership, so hadd remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود
باب الوطء الذي يوجب الحد.
ومن زنى بأمة فقتلها لزمه الحد والقيمة، والخليفة يؤخذ بالقصاص وبالأموال
بفعل الزنا أي الزاني بالزنا بالقتل
أي السلطان
إذا قتل إنسانا بغير حق
لا بالحد .
واحد منهما بالاتفاق، وفي الوجه الثاني وهو ما إذا أقر أحدهما وأنكر الآخر ولم يدع شبهة، لا يحد المنكر بالاتفاق، ويحد المقر عندهما لا عنده. (فتح) ومن زنى بأمة إلخ أي من زنى بجارية فقتلها بفعل الزنا، فإنه يحد، وعليه قيمتها؛ لأنه جنى جنايتين، فلزمه جزاء كل واحد منهما، وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يحد؛ لأن تقرر ضمان القيمة بسبب تملك الأمة فصار كما إذا اشتراها بعد ما زنى بها واعتراض سبب الملك قبل إقامة الحد يوجب سقوط الحد كما إذا ملك المسروق قبل القطع يسقط عنه القطع، ولهما: أنه ضمان قتل فلا يوجب الملك؛ لأن محل الملك قد فات، بخلاف ما إذا زنى بها فأذهب عينها بالزنا حيث يجب عليه قيمتها ويسقط الحد؛ لأن الملك قد ثبت في الجثة العمياء، فأورث الشبهة الدارئة للحد، ولو غصبها ثم زنى بها ثم ضمن قيمتها فلا حد عليه عندهم جميعاً. (مستخلص، فتح) والخليفة يؤخذ إلخ: لأنه حق العباد، فإذا قتل السلطان نفساً عمداً بغير حق، إما يمكن نفسه . أولياء المقتول، فيقتلونه، أو يستعينون عليه بمنعة المسلمين. وبالأموال: أي وكذا يؤخذ بالأموال إذا أتلف مال إنسان بغير حق فإنها من حقوق العباد أيضاً فيستوفي من ماله. لا بالحد: أي لا يؤخذ الخليفة بالحدود، والخليفة الإمام الذي ليس فوقه إمام فإذا قذف إنساناً أو شرب حمراً أو زنى لا يحد؛ لأن الحدود حق الله تعالى، وهو المكلف بإقامتها، فلا يقدر على إقامتها على نفسه؛ لأن فائدة الإقامة الزجر والزجر بإقامة الغير لا بفعل نفسه؛ إذ الإقامة بطريق الخزي والنكال ولا يفعل ذلك أحد بنفسه وفعل نائبه كفعله؛ لأنه بأمره، فإذا لم يقدر لم يشرع رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٥/١] (مستخلص) من
Book of Hudud. Chapter on Intercourse that Necessitates the Hadd. Whoever commits zina with a slave woman and kills her, upon him is the hadd and the value [of the slave woman]. And the caliph is subject to retaliation (qisas) and [liable for] financial [penalties], but not to the hadd. [Commentary:] 'by the act of zina' meaning the fornicator [kills] by the act of zina with killing; 'the caliph' meaning the sultan; 'if he kills a person without right'; 'not to the hadd'. One of them [the caliph and the common person] by agreement; in the second aspect, which is when one of them confesses and the other denies and does not claim a shubha, the denier is not punished by hadd by agreement, and the confessor is punished according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) not according to him (Abu Hanifa). (Fath) 'Whoever commits zina with a slave woman etc.' meaning whoever commits zina with a slave girl and kills her by the act of zina, then he is punished by hadd and owes her value; because he committed two offenses, so the penalty for each one is due upon him. From Abu Yusuf that he is not punished by hadd; because the establishment of the guarantee of value due to ownership of the slave woman, so it becomes as if he bought her after he committed zina with her, and the interposition of the cause of ownership before the establishment of the hadd necessitates the dropping of the hadd, just as if he owns the stolen property before amputation, amputation is dropped. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is a guarantee for killing, so it does not necessitate ownership; because the locus of ownership has perished, unlike the case where he commits zina with her and destroys her by zina, where upon him is her value and the hadd is dropped; because ownership is established in the lifeless body, thus it creates a shubha that repels the hadd. And if he dispossesses her (by force) and then commits zina with her and then guarantees her value, there is no hadd upon him according to all of them. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'And the caliph is subject etc.' because it is a right of servants. So if the sultan kills a soul intentionally without right, the heirs of the slain are either able [to retaliate] themselves, so they kill him, or they seek help from the Muslim community. 'And to financial [penalties]' meaning also he is subject to financial penalties if he destroys someone's property without right, for these are also rights of servants, so it is exacted from his wealth. 'Not to the hadd' meaning the caliph is not subject to the hudud. And the caliph is the imam above whom there is no imam. So if he slanders someone, or drinks wine, or commits zina, he is not punished by hadd; because the hudud are the right of Allah, and he is the one charged with establishing them, so he is not able to establish them upon himself; because the benefit of establishment is deterrence, and deterrence is by the establishment of another, not by his own act; since establishment is by way of disgrace and punishment, and no one does that to himself, and the act of his deputy is like his act; because it is by his command. So since he is not able, it is not legislated. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/385) (Mustakhlas) from
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses two rulings within the chapter on hudud. First: a man who commits zina with a slave woman and kills her during the act must undergo the hadd for zina and pay her market value, because he committed two separate crimes. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as stated in the text. However, Abu Yusuf holds that the hadd is dropped because the guarantee of value creates ownership of the slave woman, which becomes a shubha (doubt) that repels the hadd, analogous to buying the slave after zina or owning stolen property before amputation. The response from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that this is a guarantee for killing, which cannot establish ownership since the slave is dead; thus it differs from the case where the slave is alive after zina, where the hadd is dropped. If the slave was illegally taken and then killed after zina, all agree the hadd is dropped. Second: the caliph (imam) is subject to qisas for murder and financial penalties for property damage, but not to hudud (fixed punishments for zina, drinking, slander) because hudud are rights of Allah and he is the executor; he cannot execute them on himself, and his deputy's act is like his own. The passage includes both matn and commentary, with sources from Fath al-Qadir and Mustakhlas.

Key Terms
حد (Hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft, drinking).
شبهة (Shubha): A legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd.
ضمان (Daman): Guarantee or liability for compensation, here referring to the obligation to pay the value of the slave woman killed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is the hadd not dropped when a man kills the slave woman he has committed zina with?
A) Because the killing is a separate crime that nullifies the zina.
B) Because the guarantee for killing does not create ownership over a dead person.
C) Because the hadd for zina is always imposed regardless of circumstances.
D) Because the man can choose to pay a fine instead of facing hadd.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd for zina is dropped only when a valid shubha of ownership exists; a guarantee for killing does not create that shubha, so the hadd remains.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

The Caliph's Immunity from Hadd: Reasoning and Scope
Ruling on caliph's immunity from hadd with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the caliph is not subject to hudud punishments according to Hanafi fiqh, and apply the principle that hudud are rights of Allah that cannot be executed by the ruler on himself.

Core Idea
The caliph cannot execute hadd on himself because he is the executor of Allah's rights.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical rule of Islamic governance: the caliph (imam) is subject to qisas and financial penalties (rights of servants) but is immune from hudud (rights of Allah). The reasoning is that the caliph is the one charged with implementing hudud, and he cannot implement them on himself. This lesson explores the rationale and its implications for the ruler's accountability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the caliph
The matn states: 'The caliph is subject to retaliation and financial penalties, but not to hadd.' This is the general rule.
2
Understand the classification of rights
Hudud are rights of Allah (huquq Allah), while qisas and financial penalties are rights of servants (huquq al-ibad). This distinction determines the ruler's liability.
Hanafi fiqh separates huquq Allah from huquq al-ibad for procedural and substantive rules.
3
Analyze the rationale for immunity from hadd
The commentary explains: the caliph is the executor of hudud; he cannot execute them on himself. Deterrence requires another person to apply the punishment. The caliph's deputy's action is considered his own, so he also cannot delegate someone to do it.
4
Note the scope of immunity
The immunity covers all fixed penalties (slander, wine drinking, zina). It does not cover qisas (retaliation for murder) or financial penalties (damage to property), which are rights of victims.
The ruler can be held accountable by the victim's heirs for murder (qisas) and by courts for financial claims.
5
Apply the rule to a modern context
In a modern Islamic state, the head of state would similarly not be subject to hadd because he is the final authority for enforcement. However, he can be impeached or held accountable constitutionally for other offenses.
This rule is specific to the classical caliph; its application to modern heads of state varies by the structure of governance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بفعل الزنا أي الزاني بالزنا بالقتل

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses two rulings within the chapter on hudud. The passage includes both matn and commentary, with sources from Fath al-Qadir and Mustakhlas.

Key Terms
خليفة (Khalifah): The supreme political leader of the Muslim community; the imam with no superior ruler.
قصاص (Qisas): Retaliation; punishment by causing similar harm to the offender, specifically for murder or bodily injury.
حق الله (Haqq Allah): A right of Allah; a claim where the punishment benefits the public order and religious boundaries.
حق العبد (Haqq al-`Abd): A right of a human being; a claim that belongs to an individual, such as compensation or retaliation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the caliph not subject to hadd for drinking wine, according to the Hanafi passage?
A) Because the caliph is infallible and cannot commit sin.
B) Because the caliph is the executor of hudud and cannot execute them on himself.
C) Because drinking wine is not a hadd offense for the ruler.
D) Because the caliph can buy his way out of hadd.

Key Takeaway
The caliph's immunity from hadd is procedural: as the ultimate executor, he cannot apply hudud on himself, but he remains fully liable for personal rights like qisas and financial claims.

Delayed Testimony for Hudud: The Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on delayed testimony in hadd cases and qadhf exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delayed testimony for hudud, explain the exception for qadhf, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with evidence.

Core Idea
Delayed testimony for hudud is rejected (except qadhf) because hudud are rights of Allah, nullifiable by delay; but human rights remain.

In the chapter on testimony for zina and withdrawal, the Hanafi jurists discuss a key issue: when witnesses delay reporting a hadd crime (like zina, theft, or drinking), does their testimony still hold? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, its proof from the statement of Umar (RA), and the disagreement with other schools led by al-Shafi'i. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi distinction between rights of Allah and rights of servants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: testimony for a hadd that is delayed (taqadum). State the Hanafi ruling: the testimony is not accepted, and the hadd is not imposed, except for qadhf.
The ruling is about the acceptance of testimony, not the punishment itself.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the statement of Umar (RA): 'Any people who testify for a hadd and do not testify about it in his presence, they are witnesses of malice.' Also the principle that hudud are pure rights of Allah.
The proof is both naqli (Umar's statement) and aqli (the nature of hudud).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof supports the ruling: Umar's statement indicates that delay raises suspicion of malice, making witnesses unreliable. The principle: hudud, being rights of Allah, can be nullified by factors indicating defect (like delay), unlike human rights which are established more firmly.
This contrasts with Shafi'i reasoning that hudud are like human rights.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing school: al-Shafi'i (followed by Malik and Ahmad) holds that delay does not invalidate testimony for hudud, analogizing them to rights of servants.
This is a fundamental usul difference on the nature of hudud.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: In a Hanafi court, old hadd cases are not pursued unless there is a valid excuse, while Shafi'is would accept such testimony. This affects how cases are judged.
The thamarah is the actual difference in application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الزنا والرجوع عنها الشهادة أي في بيان أحكامها عن شهدوا بحد متقادم سوى حد القذف لم يحد، وضمن السرقة، أي المشهود عليه أي المال المسروق أي شهدت أربعة لأن فيه حق العبد باب الشهادة إلخ: قد أن الزنا يثبت إما بالبينة أو الإقرار ثم ذكر في هذا الباب أسباباً ترد بها الشهادة كالتقادم والاختلاف في الزمان والمكان والجهل بالمزني بها، وكل هذه عوارض على خلاف الأصل، فناسب تأخيرها. (فتح) شهدوا [ أي بسبب حد كسرقة أو زنا أو شرب (ط)] أي إذا شهد الشهود بحد متقادم ولم يمنعهم عن الشهادة على الفور بُعْدُهم عن الإمام، أو مرضهم أو خوف الطريق لم تقبل شهادتهم إلا في حد القذف خاصة، والأصل في هذا أن الحدود الخالصة حق الله تعالى تبطل بالتقادم عندنا، وعند الشافعي: لا تبطل كحقوق العباد، وبه قال مالك وأحمد. عورة ستر حر الله عوراته يوم ذلك عن ولنا: قول عمر ه: "أيما قوم شهدوا في حد لم يشهدوا به عند حضرته فإنما هم شهود ضغن"، ولا شهادة للمتهم، ولأن الشاهد متى عاين الزنا ونحوه فهو مخير بين أجرين أجر أداء الشهادة ليقام الحد، فيحصل الانزجار، قال تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الشَّهَادَةَ اللهِ ﴾ (الطلاق:۲)، وأجر الستر على المسلم، قال عليه: "من ستر على أخيه المسلم القيامة"، وتأخير الأداء إما أن يكون للستر، فالإقدام على الأداء بعد ذلك لضغينة تركتهم ،فيتهمون ولا شهادة للمتهم وإن كان لا للستر صاروا آئمين فاسقين بالتأخير؛ لأن أداء الشهادة من الواجبات، وتأخيرها فسق إلا أن يكون التأخير لمرض ونحوه، فتقبل إجماعاً، ثم حد التقادم شهر روي أبي يوسف ومحمد وقيل ستة أشهر، وإليه أشار الطحاوي. وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه مفوض إلى رأي القاضي والأول أصح، والتقادم في شرب الخمر أو السكر بغيرها انقطاع الرائحة خلافاً لمحمد، هو يجعله مثل غيره من الحدود، والإقرار لا يمنع بالتقادم خلافاً لزفر، وقوله: "سوى حد القذف" أي لا يمنع فيه التقادم؛ لأن فيه حق العبد، والتقادم غير مانع في حقوق العباد، ولهذا لم يصح الرجوع عنه بعد الإقرار، وقوله : " لم يحد" أي الشخص الذي تقادم الحد عليه وأما الشهود، فعند البعض يحدون والظاهر أنه لا يجب عليهم الحد؛ لأن عددهم متكامل، والأهلية للشهادة موجودة فيمنع أن يكون كلامهم قذفاً. (عيني، فتح) بحد متقادم بلا عذر كمرض أو بعد مسافة أو خوف طريق . (ط) لم يحد أي لم تقبل الشهادة ولم يحد الشخص الذي تقادم عليه الحد للتهمة (عيني) وضمن السرقة: أي إذا شهدوا بالسرقة المتقادمة لا يقطع السارق؛ لأن التقادم يمنع الشهادة بالحد للتهمة، ولا يمنع ضمان المال؛ لأنه حق العبد وهو لا يسقط بالتقادم فصار نظير ما لو شهد رجل وامرأتان بالسرقة فإنه يجب فيه المال، ولا يجب فيه القطع [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٦/١] (فتح)
Chapter on Testimony for Zina and Withdrawal Therefrom. [The chapter on] testimony, i.e., regarding its rulings. 'When they testify for a hadd that is delayed, except for the hadd of qadhf (false accusation), the hadd is not imposed, and [the witness] guarantees the theft.' i.e., the one testified against, i.e., the stolen property; i.e., four testify. Because it involves the right of a servant. The chapter on testimony etc.: indeed, zina is established either by evidence or confession. Then in this chapter, causes are mentioned by which testimony is rejected, such as delay (taqadum), difference in time and place, and ignorance of the woman with whom zina was committed. All these are incidental matters against the principle, so it is appropriate to mention them later. (Fath) 'They testify' i.e., concerning a hadd like theft, zina, or drinking (T). i.e., when witnesses testify for a hadd that is delayed, and nothing prevented them from testifying immediately (such as distance from the imam, illness, or fear of the road), their testimony is not accepted, except specifically for the hadd of qadhf. The basis for this is that pure hudud are the right of Allah and become invalid due to delay according to us (Hanafis). According to al-Shafi'i, they do not become invalid, like the rights of servants, and Malik and Ahmad said the same. 'Aura satara hurr allah awratahu yawma dhalika' (obscure text). And for us: the statement of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Any people who testify for a hadd and do not testify about it in his presence, they are witnesses of malice.' And there is no testimony for the accused. Because when a witness directly witnesses zina or similar, he is given a choice between two rewards: the reward of performing testimony so that the hadd is established and deterrence occurs (Allah said: 'And establish the testimony for Allah' (65:2)), and the reward of concealing (satara) the Muslim; he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever conceals (satara) a Muslim, Allah will conceal him on the Day of Resurrection.' And delaying the performance is either for the sake of concealment, then coming forward after that is due to malice that leaves them, so they are suspected and there is no testimony for a suspect; or if it is not for concealment, they become sinful by delaying because performing testimony is obligatory, and delaying it is fisq (sin), unless the delay is due to illness or similar, then it is accepted by consensus. Then the limit of delay (taqadum) is one month, reported from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and it is said six months, and al-Tahawi indicated that. From Abu Hanifa: it is delegated to the opinion of the judge, and the first is more correct. And the delay in the case of drinking wine or intoxication by other means is determined by the disappearance of the smell, contrary to Muhammad, who makes it like other hudud. And confession is not prevented by delay, contrary to Zufar. And his statement: 'except for the hadd of qadhf' means that delay does not prevent it because it involves the right of the servant, and delay does not prevent rights of servants; therefore withdrawal from it after confession is not valid. And his statement: 'the hadd is not imposed' means the person against whom the hadd is delayed, and as for the witnesses, according to some they are punished by hadd, but apparently they are not obligated because their number is complete and their eligibility for testimony exists, so it prevents their speech from being considered qadhf. (Ayni, Fath) 'For a hadd that is delayed without excuse like illness, distance, or fear of the road.' (T) 'The hadd is not imposed' means the testimony is not accepted and the person against whom the hadd is delayed is not punished due to suspicion. (Ayni) 'And guarantees the theft' means if they testify about an old theft, the thief is not amputated, because delay prevents testimony for the hadd due to suspicion, but it does not prevent the guarantee of wealth because it is a right of the servant and is not nullified by delay. Thus it becomes analogous to the case where one man and two women testify for theft: the wealth is obligated, but amputation is not. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/386] (Fath)
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on testimony for zina and its withdrawal addresses the effect of delay (taqadum) on the validity of testimony for hudud. The Hanafi position is that testimony for an old hadd (e.g., zina, theft, drinking) is not accepted if the delay was without valid excuse, except for the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) because it involves a human right. The proof is the statement of Umar (RA) that delayed witnesses are 'witnesses of malice', and the principle that hudud are rights of Allah which can be nullified by delay, unlike human rights. This is a point of inter-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that delay does not invalidate testimony for hudud. The text also explains that the witness is given a choice between two rewards: testifying to establish the hadd (with the command of Allah to establish testimony) and concealing the Muslim (based on hadith). If the delay was for concealment, the witness is suspected of malice; if not, he is sinful for delaying an obligation. The period of delay that prevents testimony is disputed: one month (from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), six months, or left to the judge (from Abu Hanifa). For wine drinking, the delay is determined by disappearance of smell (according to Abu Hanifa), while Muhammad considers it like other hudud. Confession is not prevented by delay. Additionally, if witnesses testify for an old theft, the thief is not amputated but must pay the value, because the financial right is a human right not nullified by delay. The passage ends noting that the witnesses themselves are not punished for qadhf because their number (four) and eligibility prevent their testimony from being considered false accusation.

Key Terms
تقادم (taqadum): The delay of testimony from the time of the crime until a later time without a valid excuse.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; the hadd for qadhf is 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadd of qadhf excepted from the rule that delayed testimony is invalid?
A) Because qadhf is a lesser crime
B) Because qadhf involves a human right, which is not nullified by delay
C) Because the punishment for qadhf is light
D) Because qadhf is not a fixed punishment

Key Takeaway
Delayed testimony for a hadd (without a valid excuse) is rejected in the Hanafi school, except for qadhf, because hudud are rights of Allah which can be nullified by factors like delay, whereas human rights are not.

Outdated Testimony in Hudud: The Hanafi Position
States the basic rule with proof and rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on outdated testimony in hudud and explain the proof from Umar's statement.

Core Idea
Delayed hudud testimony is rejected due to suspicion of spite, except qadhf which involves a personal right.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on testimony that is brought forward long after a hadd crime occurred. The school holds that without a valid excuse, such testimony is rejected because the delay raises doubt about the witnesses' motives. We will explore the proof from the Companion Umar and the rationale behind distinguishing pure divine rights from personal rights.

Guided Path
1
State the Basic Ruling
Identify the core ruling: if witnesses testify about an outdated hadd (e.g., zina, theft, drinking) without a valid excuse, their testimony is not accepted, except for qadhf (false accusation).
The phrase 'without excuse' is critical; delays due to illness, distance, or fear are valid.
2
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
Read the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'Any people who testify regarding a hadd penalty but did not testify in its presence, they are witnesses of spite.' Understand that this labels delayed witnesses as suspects, thus rejecting their testimony.
The saying is considered zanni in transmission, but accepted as a basis for the ruling.
3
Understand the Rationale
The witness originally has two rewards: for testifying or for covering a sin. Delaying without cause implies either spite (if now testifying) or sin (if not covering). In either case, the witness becomes suspect and their testimony invalid.
If delay is for covering, later testimony is spite; if not, the witness is a sinner (fasiq), so testimony rejected.
4
Note the Exception
Qadhf is exempt because it involves the right of the accused (a personal right), not a pure divine right. Taqadum does not bar personal rights.
This distinction is fundamental: pure hudud (rights of Allah) expire with time, but personal rights do not.
5
Compare with Other Schools
Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali do not recognize taqadum as a bar, analogizing hudud to personal rights. Hanafi response: the hadd is a divine right, and delay indicates suspicion.
The practical difference: under Hanafi, a late-reported theft avoids amputation but property is returned; under Shafi'i, amputation could still be applied.

Commentary
This passage is a complex legal ruling on the effect of delayed testimony in hudud penalties. It opens with the basic ruling: if witnesses come forward with testimony about a hadd crime that occurred long ago, without a valid excuse like distance, illness, or fear of the road, their testimony is rejected—except for the hadd of false accusation (qadhf). The reason is that pure hudud are rights of Allah that are invalidated by antiquity according to the Hanafi school, unlike the rights of individuals. The proof is Umar's statement labeling such witnesses as 'witnesses of spite,' making them accused. The text then explains that the witness has a choice between two rewards: testifying to establish the hadd or concealing the sin. Delaying the testimony without a valid excuse makes the witness a sinner, so coming forward later makes them suspect. The duration considered as 'taqadum' is disputed within the Hanafi school: one month according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, six months according to others, and Abu Hanifa leaves it to the judge's discretion. For intoxication, the period is until the odor wears off, differing from Muhammad who treats it like other hudud. Confession is not affected by antiquity, contrary to Zufar. The passage then clarifies that 'except qadhf' means antiquity does not bar the hadd because it involves a personal right. Finally, it addresses the case of outdated theft testimony: the thief is not amputated due to suspicion, but must return the stolen property because that is a personal right that does not expire.

Key Terms
تقادم (taqadum): The passage of time sufficient to render testimony suspect; a legal impediment to accepting testimony in hudud
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment for false accusation of zina, which is 80 lashes
