Six Cases Where Hadd for Drinking is Averted
Expansion of six conditions averting hadd for drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six scenarios where the hadd for drinking is not applied and explain the Hanafi reasoning behind each, including the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between the two shaykhs and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Doubts (shubuhāt) avert hudud, specifically the absence of smell, possibility of coercion, and intoxication.

The hadd for drinking wine is established when certain conditions are met, but Islamic law is built on the principle of averting punishments in the presence of doubts. This passage from Kanz al-Daqā'iq presents six specific scenarios where the hadd is not applied, highlighting the reasoning of the early Hanafi masters and their differences. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for proper application of the hadd and reflects the school's commitment to protecting the accused through rigorous evidentiary standards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle of shubuhāt
Begin by recognizing that the six scenarios all involve a form of doubt (shubhah) that prevents the hadd. This is a foundational Hanafi principle: hudud are averted by doubts.
The principle is derived from the hadith 'Idra'ū al-ḥudūd bi al-shubuhāt'.
2
Analyze the first two scenarios: confession and testimony after smell disappears
In both cases, the smell of wine has vanished by the time the confession is made or testimony is given. Understand the split between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The two shaykhs rely on the reported consensus of the Companions that included Ibn Mas'ud's condition of smell; Muhammad analogizes to zina where confession is valid regardless of time lapse.
3
Examine scenarios three and four: detection of smell and vomiting without confession or testimony
When only the smell is detected, or the person vomits wine, without any admission or witness, the hadd is not applied because alternative explanations (e.g., eating quince, coercion) create doubt.
These scenarios highlight the requirement for a clear, unambiguous basis for the punishment.
4
Consider scenario five: retraction of confession
If a person confesses then retracts, the retraction is accepted due to the possibility of truth, and the hadd is averted.
This is consistent with the principle that retraction is accepted in pure divine right penalties.
5
Study scenario six and the definition of intoxication
Confession while completely intoxicated (loss of intellect) is not valid, as it carries high risk of falsehood. Note the two definitions of intoxication: Abu Hanifa's (complete loss of intellect) vs. the two's (mixing jest and seriousness). The majority follows the latter.
This scenario leads into the broader discussion of the legal capacity of an intoxicated person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أقر أو شهدا: هذا شرط يتضمن ست مسائل، والجزاء قوله: "لا" أي لا يحد في المسائل الست: الأولى: أنه أقر بشرب الخمر وقد انعدمت رائحتها لا يحد عند الشيخين خلافاً لمحمد؛ لأن التقادم لا يبطل صحة الإقرار كما في حد الزنا، ولهما: أن حد الشرب ثبت بإجماع الصحابة، والإجماع بدون رأي ابن مسعود لا يتم، وقد أنه يشترط الرائحة ولم يوجد الشرط. الثانية: لو شهد رجلان بعد مضي ريح الخمر على شربه فلا يحد عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وقيد بقوله : "لا لبعد المسافة؛ لأن زوال الرائحة لبعد المسافة لا يمنع الحد. الثالثة: أنه وجد منه رائحة الخمر بلا شهادة ولا إقرار، فلا يحد؛ لأن الرائحة قد تكون من غير الخمر كالسفرجلة. الرابعة: أنه تقيأ الخمر من غير شهادة وإقرار لا يحد؛ لأنه يحتمل أنه شربها مكرهاً أو مضطراً فلا يجب بالشك. الخامسة: أنه أقر بشرب الخمر ثم رجع عن إقراره لا يحد؛ لاحتمال أنه صادق في رجوعه دون إقراره. السادسة : أنه أقر في حالة السكر بأن زال عقله، ولا يعرف الأرض من السماء، ولا الرجال من النساء، ولا يعرف شيئاً، وهذا التفسير عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما السكران من يختلط جده بهزله ويهذي، وعليه أكثر المشايخ وعند الشافعي المعتبر ظهور أثر السكر في مشيه وحركاته وأطرافه. فلو أقر من زال عقله بأنه شرب الخمر لا يحد؛ لزيادة احتمال الكذب في إقراره فيحتال لدرئه، ودلّ كلام وهو قوله: "أو أقر سكران أن إقراره حال السكر بالحدود الخالصة حق الله تعالى غير صحيح، فيعمل الرجوع فيه، وأما غير الخالصة كحد القذف فيصح، وعرف منه أن إقراره بحقوق العباد الخالصة مثل القصاص والأموال والنكاح في السكر صحيح بالأولى، ولهذا لو أقر بالسرقة أخذ منه المال، ولم يقطع، بخلاف الإقرار بحد القذف والقصاص وغيرهما من حقوق العباد؛ لأنه لا يحتمل الرجوع، وبخلاف ما إذا زنى أو سرق أو شرب في حالة السكر حيث يجب عليه الحد، وهذا إذا سكر بالمحرم، وأما إذا سكر بالمباح كشرب المضطر والمكره والمتخذ من الحبوب والعسل والدواء، فلا تعتبر تصرفاته كلها؛ لأنه بمنزلة الإغماء. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) لا: أي لم يكن تأخيرهم عن الشهادة لبعد المكان. (عيني) بأن زال: تفسير المسكر وهو أن لا يعرف الرجل من المرأة ولا الأرض من السماء ولا يعرف شيئاً. (ط، عيني) لا : أي لا يجب الحد في هذه الصور كلها. (ط)
And if he confesses or two witnesses testify: this is a condition that includes six issues, and the penalty is his saying 'no', meaning he is not punished in the six issues: First: that he confessed to drinking wine and its smell has disappeared—he is not punished according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad, because lapse of time does not invalidate the validity of confession as in the hadd of zina. And for the two shaykhs: the hadd for drinking was established by consensus of the Companions, and consensus without the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud is not complete, and he (Ibn Mas'ud) stipulated the smell and the condition was not found. Second: If two men testify after the smell of wine has passed about his drinking, then he is not punished according to them (the two shaykhs), contrary to Muhammad, and he restricted it by saying 'not due to distance', because the disappearance of smell due to distance does not prevent the hadd. Third: That the smell of wine is detected from him without testimony or confession—he is not punished, because the smell may come from other than wine, like quince. Fourth: That he vomited wine without testimony or confession—he is not punished, because it is possible that he drank it under coercion or necessity, so it is not obligatory due to doubt. Fifth: That he confessed to drinking wine then retracted his confession—he is not punished, because it is possible that he is truthful in his retraction rather than his confession. Sixth: That he confessed while intoxicated to the extent that his intellect had left him, and he does not know the earth from the sky, nor men from women, nor does he know anything. This interpretation is according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the intoxicated person is one whose seriousness mixes with his jesting and he raves, and upon this is the majority of the mashayikh. According to al-Shafi'i, the criterion is the appearance of the effect of intoxication in his walking, movements, and limbs. If one whose intellect has left him confesses to drinking wine, he is not punished due to the increased possibility of lying in his confession, so it is used as a stratagem to avert it. And his statement indicates: 'or an intoxicated person confessed that his confession while intoxicated concerning pure hadd punishments of Allah is not valid, so retraction is accepted, but concerning impure ones like the hadd for qadhf it is valid.' From this it is understood that his confession concerning pure rights of servants like retaliation, money, and marriage while intoxicated is valid a fortiori, and therefore if he confessed to theft, the money is taken from him but he is not amputated, unlike confession to the hadd of qadhf, retaliation, and other rights of servants because it does not bear retraction, and unlike if he committed zina, theft, or drinking while intoxicated where the hadd is obligatory upon him. This is if he became intoxicated with something prohibited, but if he became intoxicated with something permissible like the drink of one compelled, coerced, or made from grains, honey, or medicine, then all his actions are not considered because he is like one unconscious. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) 'La': meaning their delay in testimony was not due to distance of place. (Ayni) 'Bi an zal': interpretation of the intoxicating substance, that he does not recognize the man from the woman nor the earth from the sky nor does he know anything. (T, Ayni) 'La': meaning the hadd is not obligatory in all these scenarios. (T)
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the conditions that avert the hadd punishment for drinking wine. The author presents six scenarios divided between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) versus Muhammad al-Shaybani. The core principle is that doubts (shubuhāt) avert hudud. The first two scenarios involve the disappearance of the smell of wine before confession or testimony. The two shaykhs hold that if the smell is gone, the hadd is not applied because the consensus of the Companions included a condition from Ibn Mas'ud that the smell must be present. Muhammad disagrees, arguing that confession is valid regardless of smell, like in zina. The third scenario: only smell is detected without testimony or confession—not punished because smell may not be from wine. Fourth: vomiting wine without confession—not punished because it could have been under duress. Fifth: retraction of confession—not punished due to possibility of truth. Sixth: confession while completely intoxicated (intellect gone)—not punished due to high possibility of falsehood. The passage then distinguishes between pure rights of Allah and mixed rights: for pure divine penalties, the intoxicated person's confession is invalid and retraction is accepted; for mixed penalties like theft or retaliation, confession is valid for the financial aspect but not for amputation or criminal penalty. Finally, a distinction is made between intoxication from prohibited substances (where all actions are considered) and from permitted substances (like medicine) where the person is like unconscious and his actions are null.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; acknowledgment of guilt by the accused.
ريح الخمر (rih al-khamr): The smell of wine; a necessary condition for establishing the hadd according to Ibn Mas'ud's view.
سكران (sakran): An intoxicated person; legal definitions vary: Abu Hanifa says one who loses intellect; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say one whose seriousness mixes with jesting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which scenario does the hadd for drinking NOT apply according to the two shaykhs?
A) When the person confesses immediately after drinking with the smell still present.
B) When two witnesses testify after the smell has disappeared.
C) When the person vomits wine and then confesses.
D) When the person drinks while intoxicated and confesses after sobering up.

Key Takeaway
Six specific doubts (absent smell, lack of direct evidence, retraction, and intoxication) prevent the application of the hadd for drinking, reflecting the Hanafi principle of caution in hudud.

Hadd al-Shurb: 80 Lashes, Evidence, and Application
Ruling on punishment amount, evidence, and procedural details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the hadd for drinking, explain the evidence from hadith and consensus, and identify the differences for slaves and the distribution method.

Core Idea
The hadd for drinking is 80 lashes for a free person, based on qiyas with qadhf and the practice of the Companions.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq establishes the punishment for drinking wine and other intoxicants as eighty lashes. It provides the Hanafi proof from the Prophet's hadith linking drinking to slander (qadhf), which carries eighty lashes. The author also addresses the dispute with the Shafi'i school, who hold for forty lashes, and details the application: half for slaves, distribution over the body, and whether to strip the drinker.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage defines the hadd for intoxication (sukr) and drinking wine as eighty lashes. Determine the subject (free person) and the punishment.
The term 'sukr' here refers to intoxicants other than wine, but the same ruling applies to wine.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith from al-Daraqutni: 'When he drinks, he becomes intoxicated; when intoxicated, he raves; when he raves, he slanders; and the slanderer gets 80 lashes.' This links drinking to qadhf, which has 80 lashes in the Quran.
Also, consensus of the Companions and the practice of Uthman are cited.
3
Trace the response to the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i cites the Prophet's practice with palm branches and sandals, and Abu Bakr's 40 lashes. The Hanafi response is that each blow with a branch/sandal counted as two strokes, making the total 80.
This is supported by Abu Sa'id's report that Umar replaced each sandal with a whip.
4
Note the difference for slaves
For a slave, the hadd is half: 40 lashes. This is based on the practice of Umar and ibn Umar flogging their slaves half the hadd, and the principle that slavery reduces certain penalties.
The text also mentions that slavery is a factor in reducing the punishment.
5
Examine the distribution and stripping
The lashes must be distributed over the body to avoid harm, just like in zina. For stripping, the well-known Hanafi position is to remove the drinker's clothes (except covering), while Muhammad holds not to strip to show leniency.
The places to avoid are the head, face, and private parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحد السكر: بضم السين وسكون الكاف والمراد من هذا السكر بغير الخمر بدليل عطف الخمر عليه، وبناء الحكم الآخر على الخمر، وهو قوله: "ولو شرب" "قطرة لإطلاق" قوله عليه: "من شرب الخمر فاجلدوه"، وقوله: "ثمانون سوطاً" خبر المبتدأ أي حد السكر من غير الخمر وحد شرب الخمر ولو قليلا ثمانون سوطاً عندنا، وقال الشافعي وأحمد: أربعون، لما روي عن أنس له أن النبي عليه ضرب في الخمر بالجريد والنعال، وضرب أبو بكر له أربعين، وبه قال أحمد في رواية ولنا: قول عليه "أنه إذا شرب سكر، وإذا سكر هذي، وإذا هذي افترى، وعلى المفتري أي القاذف ثمانون جلدة في كتاب الله تعالى"، رواه الدار قطني. ومالك بمعناه، وعليه إجماع الصحابة، وما رواه كان بجريدتين والنعلين فكان كل ضربة بضربتين فكان حجة لنا، والذي يدلك على هذا قول أبي سعيد: "جلد على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الخمر بنعلين، فلما كان في زمن عمر جعل بدل كل نعل سوطاً"، رواه أحمد، وفي الصحيح أن عثمان وعبد الله بن عمر أمر علياً له أن يجلد الوليد ثمانين. رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۲/۱] (فتح) ولو شرب متصلة أي ولو شرب منها قطرة. (عيني) و للعبد :نصفه أي حد السكر وحد شربة الخمر في حق العبد نصف ثمانين، لرواية الموطأ: أن عمر وعبد الله بن عمر جلدوا عبيدهم نصف الحد في الخمر؛ ولأن الرق منصف، وقوله: "وفرق على بدنه كحد الزنا" أي يفرق الضرب على أعضاء الشارب كما في حد الزنا؛ لأن الجمع في موضع واحد قد يؤدي إلى الهلاك، وهل يجرد الشارب عن ثيابه؟ فالمشهور عن أصحابنا أنه ينزع عنه الفرو والحشو ويجرد عن ثيابه؛ لأن سببه متيقن به كحد الزنا، بخلاف حد القذف؛ لأن سببه غير متيقن به؛ لاحتمال أن يكون القاذف صادقاً فيه، وعن محمد: لا يجرد؛ إظهاراً للتخفيف؛ لأنه لم يرد به نص قطعي، وإنما يثبت بالإجماع، وجه المشهور أنا قد أظهرنا التخفيف مرة في التفريق والعدد فلا يعتبر كحد تنبيه على أنه يتوقى المواضع التي استثنيت في حد الزنا وهي الرأس والوجه والفرج. (عيني) ثانياً. (مستخلص، عيني)
And the hadd of intoxication (sukr) with a damma on the sin and sukun on the kaf, and what is meant by this intoxication is other than wine, as indicated by the conjunction of wine with it, and the building of the other ruling on wine, and that is his saying: 'and if he drinks a drop for the generality of his saying: Whoever drinks wine, flog him', and his saying: 'eighty lashes' is the predicate of the subject, meaning the hadd of intoxication from other than wine and the hadd of drinking wine even if a little is eighty lashes according to us. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: forty, due to what was narrated from Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) struck in the case of wine with palm branches and sandals, and Abu Bakr struck forty, and Ahmad said it in one narration. And we have the saying (of the Prophet): 'When he drinks, he becomes intoxicated; when he becomes intoxicated, he raves; when he raves, he slanders, and upon the slanderer (i.e., the qadif) is eighty lashes in the Book of Allah.' This was narrated by al-Daraqutni. Malik said something similar, and upon it is the consensus of the Companions. And what he narrated was with two palm branches and two sandals, so each blow counted as two strokes, so it was an evidence for us. What indicates this is the saying of Abu Sa'id: 'Flogging was done at the time of the Messenger of Allah for wine with two sandals, then in the time of Umar, each sandal was replaced by a whip.' This was narrated by Ahmad. And in Sahih, Uthman and Abdullah ibn Umar ordered Ali to flog al-Walid eighty. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/392) (Fath) 'And if he drinks' is connected, meaning even if he drinks a drop from it. (Ayni) 'And for the slave: half of it', meaning the hadd of intoxication and the hadd of drinking wine in the case of a slave is half of eighty, due to the narration from Muwatta that Umar and Abdullah ibn Umar flogged their slaves half the hadd for wine, and because slavery is half. And his saying: 'and distributed over his body like the hadd of zina', meaning the lashes are distributed over the limbs of the drinker as in the hadd of zina, because concentrating in one place may lead to destruction. Should the drinker be stripped of his clothes? The well-known from our companions is that the fur and padding are removed and he is stripped of his clothes, because its cause is certain like the hadd of zina, unlike the hadd of qadhf because its cause is not certain due to the possibility that the slanderer might be truthful. From Muhammad: he should not be stripped, to show leniency, because it is not established by a definitive text but only by consensus. The face of the well-known view is that we have shown leniency once in distribution and number, so it is not considered. As a note: the places that are exempted in the hadd of zina are avoided: the head, face, and private parts. (Ayni) Second. (Mustakhlas, Ayni)
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage establishes the punishment for drinking wine (and other intoxicants) as eighty lashes for a free person. The author clarifies that the term 'sukr' here refers to intoxicants other than wine, while wine itself is also punished with eighty lashes. This is the Hanafi position, based on the hadith from al-Daraqutni that links drinking to slander (qadhf), which carries eighty lashes in the Quran. The text then addresses the dispute: Shafi'i and Ahmad hold that the punishment is forty lashes, citing the practice of Abu Bakr and the Prophet's use of palm branches and sandals. The Hanafi response is that each stroke with a branch or sandal counted as two strokes, so the actual number of lashes was effectively eighty. This is supported by the practice of Uthman flogging al-Walid eighty lashes. For a slave, the punishment is half: forty lashes, based on the practice of Umar and ibn Umar, and the principle that slavery reduces certain penalties. The lashes must be distributed over the body to avoid harm, just like in zina. The passage also discusses whether the drinker should be stripped of clothes: the well-known Hanafi position is that he is stripped (except for covering), because the cause is certain, unlike qadhf. Muhammad holds he should not be stripped to show leniency. The preferred view is that since leniency has already been shown in distribution and number, stripping is not excessive. Finally, sensitive areas (head, face, private parts) are avoided.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (hadd al-shurb): The fixed punishment for drinking alcohol: 80 lashes for free, 40 for slave.
سكر (sukr): Intoxication, here used for intoxicants other than wine.
تجريد (tajrid): Stripping of clothes for flogging; the well-known Hanafi position is to strip.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a free person who drinks wine?
A) 40 lashes
B) 80 lashes
C) 100 lashes
D) Discretionary punishment (ta'zir)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds 80 lashes for drinking, based on qiyas with qadhf and Companion consensus, with half for slaves and careful distribution.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Punishment for Drinking Wine: 80 Lashes and Its Proofs
Ruling with proof: establishes 80 lashes for drinking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the hadd of drinking wine, identify the key proofs (dalil naqli), and explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding stripping the offender.

Core Idea
The hadd for drinking is 80 lashes, established by the consensus of the Companions and the link to slander.

This lesson examines the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking wine (khamr) according to the Hanafi school. The text from Kanz al-Daqaiq states the ruling and its proofs, including the famous hadith linking drinking to slander, the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the consensus of the Companions. We will also explore the internal Hanafi disagreement about whether the offender should be stripped before lashes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Note the ruling: 80 lashes for free, 40 for slave, and that it applies even for a drop. This is the core ruling.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The passage cites a hadith from al-Daraqutni linking drinking to slander (ifra'), thus the same punishment as qadhf (80 lashes). Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the parallel drawn between the two crimes.
The hadith: 'When he drinks, he becomes intoxicated; when intoxicated, he raves; when he raves, he slanders.'
3
Consider the secondary proofs
The passage mentions the practice of the Prophet (using two sandals) and later Caliphs (using whips), and the consensus of the Companions. Analyze how each strengthens the ruling.
The practice of Abu Sa'id and the actions of 'Uthman and 'Ali.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on stripping
The well-known view is to strip the offender (except for fur and padding), while Imam Muhammad holds not to strip. Understand the rationale: certainty of sin vs. leniency.
The text says 'mashhur' vs. Muhammad's view.
5
Apply the ruling to the distinction between hadd and ta'zir
Note that the Hanafi school treats this as a hadd, not ta'zir. This has implications for proof requirements and the fixed nature of the penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود
باب حد الشرب
ولو شرب قطرةً ثمانون سوطاً، وللعبد نصفه، وفرق على بدنه كحد الزنا.
للحر عندنا أي لأجله الثمانين أي ضرب الثمانين
أربعين، وبه قال أحمد في رواية ولنا: قول عليه "أنه إذا شرب سكر، وإذا سكر هذي، وإذا هذي افترى، وعلى المفتري أي القاذف ثمانون جلدة في كتاب الله تعالى"، رواه الدار قطني.
ومالك بمعناه، وعليه إجماع الصحابة، وما رواه كان بجريدتين والنعلين فكان كل ضربة بضربتين فكان حجة لنا، والذي يدلك على هذا قول أبي سعيد: "جلد" على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الخمر بنعلين، فلما كان في زمن ه جعل بدل كل نعل سوطاً"، رواه أحمد، وفي الصحيح أن عثمان [رضي الله عنه؟] أمر علياً [رضي الله عنه؟] أن يجلد الوليد ثمانين.
(فتح) ولو شرب متصلة أي ولو شرب منها قطرة. (عيني)
و للعبد :نصفه أي حد السكر وحد شربة الخمر في حق العبد نصف ثمانين، لرواية الموطأ: أن عمر [رضي الله عنه؟] جلدوا عبيدهم نصف الحد في الخمر؛ ولأن الرق منصف، وقوله: "وفرق على بدنه كحد الزنا" أي يفرق الضرب على أعضاء الشارب كما في حد الزنا؛ لأن الجمع في موضع واحد قد يؤدي إلى الهلاك، وهل يجرد الشارب عن ثيابه؟ فالمشهور عن أصحابنا أنه ينزع عنه الفرو والحشو ويجرد عن ثيابه؛ لأن سببه متیقن به كحد الزنا، بخلاف حد القذف؛ لأن سببه غير متيقن به؛ لاحتمال أن يكون القاذف صادقاً فيه، وعن محمد: لا يجرد؛ إظهاراً للتخفيف؛ لأنه لم يرد به نص قطعي، وإنما يثبت بالإجماع، وجه المشهور أنا قد أظهرنا التخفيف مرة في التفريق والعدد فلا يعتبر كحد تنبيه على أنه يتوقى المواضع التي استثنيت في حد الزنا وهي الرأس والوجه والفرج. (عيني)
The Book of Hudud. Chapter on the Punishment for Drinking. And if he drinks a drop, eighty lashes, and for the slave half of it, and distributed over his body like the hadd for zina. For the free man according to us, i.e., for his sake the eighty, meaning the striking of eighty. Forty, and Ahmad said in a narration: and we have: a statement upon him: 'Indeed when he drinks he becomes intoxicated, and when he becomes intoxicated he raves, and when he raves he slanders, and upon the slanderer (i.e., the one who accuses falsely) is eighty lashes in the Book of Allah Almighty.' Reported by al-Daraqutni. And Malik said something similar, and upon it is the consensus of the Companions. And what he narrated was with two palm branches and two sandals, so each blow was two strikes, so it was an argument for us. And what points you to this is the statement of Abu Sa'id: 'He lashed in the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for wine with two sandals; then when it was in the time of ... he made in place of each sandal a whip.' Reported by Ahmad. And in the Sahih that 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him?) ordered 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him?) to lash al-Walid eighty. (Fath) 'And if he drinks connectedly, i.e., even if he drinks a drop from it.' (Ayni) 'And for the slave: half of it, i.e., the hadd for intoxication and the hadd for drinking wine regarding the slave is half of eighty, due to the narration of al-Muwatta' that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him?) lashed their slaves with half the hadd for wine; and because servitude is half. And his saying: 'And distributed over his body like the hadd for zina' means the beating is distributed over the limbs of the drinker as in the hadd for zina; because gathering in one place may lead to destruction. And is the drinker stripped of his clothes? The well-known view from our companions is that he is removed from the fur and padding and stripped of his clothes; because its cause is certain like the hadd for zina, unlike the hadd for slander; because its cause is not certain, due to the possibility that the slanderer may be truthful in it. And from Muhammad: he is not stripped, as a manifestation of leniency; because no definitive text came about it, but it is established by consensus. The basis of the well-known view is that we have shown leniency once in distribution and number, so it is not considered like a hadd. A reminder that he avoids the places excepted in the hadd for zina, which are the head, face, and private parts. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on the punishment for drinking. It states the Hanafi position that the hadd for drinking wine is eighty lashes for a free person and half that for a slave, and it must be distributed over the body just as in the hadd for zina, to avoid injury. The proof includes several hadiths: one narrated by al-Daraqutni linking drinking to slander and thus applying the same penalty; the practice of the Companions, including the consensus of the Sahaba; and specifically the hadith of Abu Sa'id where the Prophet used two sandals, which later Caliphs replaced with whips. There is also mention of Imam Ahmad agreeing in one narration. The passage then discusses the issue of stripping the offender: the well-known Hanafi view is that he is stripped except for fur and padding, like in zina, while Imam Muhammad holds that he is not stripped to show leniency. The passage ends by reminding that the vulnerable parts (head, face, genitals) are avoided.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (ḥadd al-shurb): The fixed punishment for consuming intoxicants (specifically wine) that leads to intoxication.
إجماع الصحابة (ijmā‘ al-ṣaḥābah): The consensus of the Companions of the Prophet, used as evidence for the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Eighty lashes
C) One hundred lashes
D) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixed the hadd for drinking wine at 80 lashes for a free person based on the link to slander (qadhf) and the consensus of the Companions.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
The Hadd for Slander (Qadhf): Conditions and Proof
Defines the hadd for slander with conditions and procedural rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of qadhf, identify the conditions for its application, and explain the Hanafi position on proof (two witnesses vs. four).

Core Idea
The hadd for slander is 80 lashes, like drinking, but only if the accused is chaste and demands it.

Slander (qadhf) is a serious crime in Islamic law, carrying a fixed punishment (hadd) of 80 lashes. However, this penalty is not automatic; it requires specific conditions regarding the accuser, the accused, and the manner of accusation. In this lesson, we will unpack the Hanafi ruling on qadhf, its conditions, and the evidence from the Quran and analogy with the punishment for drinking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that qadhf is the act of falsely accusing a chaste person of zina. The punishment (hadd) is 80 lashes, established by Quran 24:4 and analogous to the hadd for drinking.
The ruling is 'wajib' as a fixed penalty.
2
List the conditions for the hadd
Identify that the accused must be muhsan (free, adult, Muslim, chaste), the accusation must be explicit (sarih, e.g., 'O zani!'), and the accused must request the punishment. Also, the slanderer must be unable to prove the accusation with four witnesses.
Conditions prevent the hadd if the accused is not muhsan or if the accusation is indirect (kinayah).
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is Quran 24:4, which commands lashing those who accuse chaste women without four witnesses. The Hadith also supports that the punishment is 80 lashes, and analogy with the hadd for drinking (shurb) establishes the quantity and mode of proof.
The Hanafi school uses analogy (qiyas) to extend the ruling from male accusers to female accusers and from adult to minor if the accused is muhsan.
4
Understand procedural rules
The judge must ask witnesses about the place and time of the slander, and verify that the accusation was explicit. The slanderer is given time to produce witnesses (until end of session, according to the majority; Abu Yusuf says postpone to next session). The hadd is not applied if the accused is mute or unable to demand punishment.
The hadd is not nullified by lapse of time, unlike other hudud.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is a disagreement on the time given to the slanderer to produce witnesses: the majority view (mufta bihi) is until the end of the current session, while Abu Yusuf holds it should be postponed to the second session.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد القذف
أي في بيان أحكامه
هو كحد الشرب كميّةً وثبوتاً، فلو قذف محصناً أو محصنة بزنا حد بطلبه أي رجل أو امرأة أي رجلا محصنا أي امرأة محصنة أي القاذف المقذوف لأنه حقه
القذف: [وشرعاً: الرمي بالزنا وهو من الكبائر بإجماع الأمة إذا كان المقذوف محصناً وإلا فمن الصغائر. (فتح)] وهو في اللغة: الرمي مطلقا، ومنه القذافة للمقلاع، وفي القاموس التقاذف الترامي، وفي الشرع: رمي مخصوص وهو الرمي بالزنا صريحا، وهو الموجب للحد، وشرط حد القذف إحصان المقذوف، وعجز القاذف عن إثباته بالبينة، ولو قال لي بينة حاضرة في المصر أمهله القاضي إلى آخر المجلس، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يؤخره إلى المجلس الثاني. وأخر حد القذف عن حد الشرب؛ لأن جريمة الشارب متيقن بها بخلاف جريمة القاذف، فإن القذف خبر محتمل للصدق والكذب والمناسبة بينهما أن حد القذف مثل حد الشرب. (عيني، معدن)
هو عن عن كحد الشرب: أي حد القذف مثل حد الشرب في كونه ثمانين جلدة، وفي كونه ثابتاً بشهادة رجلين، ويسألهما القاضي عن القذف ما هو؟ وكيف هو؟ فإن قالا نشهد أنه قال له يا زاني، قبلت شهادتهما، وحد القاذف إن كانا عدلين وينبغي أن يسألهما . المكان؛ لاحتمال أن يكون قذفه في دار الحرب، أو دار البغي، وعن الزمان؛ لاحتمال أن يكون قذفه في صباه لا لاحتمال التقادم؛ لأن حد القذف لا يبطل به، بخلاف سائر الحدود، ويشترط اتفاق الشاهدين على اللغة التي وقع القذف بها بالاتفاق، والأصل فيه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً (النور:٤) (مستخلص، فتح) وثبوتاً: أي من الثبوت يثبت بشهادة رجلين كحد الشرب ولا تسمع فيه شهادة النساء أو يقر القاذف مرة. (ط، عيني) فلو قذف محصناً أو محصنة: أما كون المقذوف محصناً أو محصنة، فبالنص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ ﴾ الآية، ويشترط في المقذوف تصور الزنا منه بأن لا يكون محبوباً أو عنيناً أو خصياً، ولا تكون المرأة رتقا، فإن القذف فيهم لا يوجب الحد، ويشترط أن لا يكون المقذوف أخرس، فإن قذفه لا يوجب الحد؛ لأن الحد بالطلب، وطلبه بالإشارة فيحتمل أنه لو كان ينطق لصدق القاذف، وقوله: "بزنا" أي يشترط أن يكون القذف الزنا، فلو قذفه بالكنايات والتعريض لا يحد بأن قال رجل للرجل المحصن: "يا زاني"، وقال آخر: "صدقت" يحد القائل دون المصدق، ولو قال: جامعت فلانة حراماً أو فجرت بها ونحوهما لا يجب عليه الحد؛ لأن الجماع الحرام قد يكون بنكاح فاسد، وصريح الزنا من أي لسان كان يوجب الحد. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) حد بطلبه : قيد "بطلبه" لأنه لو لم يطالبه لا يحد؛ لأن فيه حقه من حيث دفع العار، لا يقال: مطالبة المقذوف ليس بشرط، فإنه يحد بمطالبة من يقع القدح في نسبه إذا كان المقذوف ميتاً كابنه؛ لأنا نقول: إنه قائم مقامه، فأخذ حكم مطالبته حكم مطالبة المقذوف فإن قيل: حق الله غالب فكان ينبغي أن لا يشترط الطلب، قلنا: حق العبد وإن كان مغلوباً فيه، لكنه يصلح أن يكون المطالبة شرطاً احتيالاً للدراً. (مستخلص، فتح)
Chapter on the Punishment for Slander (Qadhf). i.e., on explaining its rulings. It is like the punishment for drinking in quantity and proof. So if he slanders a muhsan (chaste) man or a muhsana woman with zina, he is punished upon his request (i.e., the slanderer is punished upon the request of the accused), whether it is a man or a woman, i.e., a muhsan man or a muhsana woman, i.e., the slanderer and the slandered, because it is his right. Qadhf: [and legally: accusing of zina, and it is among the major sins by consensus of the Ummah if the accused is muhsan, otherwise it is among the minor sins. (Fath)] And it is linguistically: throwing absolutely, from which is al-qadhafa for the sling, and in al-Qamus al-taqadhuf is mutual throwing. And legally: a specific throwing, which is accusing of zina explicitly, and it is what obligates the hadd. And the condition for the hadd of qadhf is the ihsan (chastity) of the accused, and the inability of the slanderer to prove it with evidence. And if he says 'I have witnesses present in the city,' the judge gives him time until the end of the session. And from Abu Yusuf: he postpones it to the second session. And the hadd for qadhf is placed after the hadd for drinking because the crime of the drinker is certain, unlike the crime of the slanderer, for slander is a report that may be true or false, and the appropriateness between them is that the hadd for qadhf is like the hadd for drinking. (Ayni, Ma'din) 'It is like the hadd for drinking' means the hadd for qadhf is like the hadd for drinking in being eighty lashes, and in being established by the testimony of two men, and the judge asks them about the slander: what it is and how it was. If they say 'We testify that he said to him: O zani!' their testimony is accepted, and the slanderer is punished if they are just. And he should ask them about the place, because it is possible that he slandered him in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy; and about the time, because it is possible that he slandered him in his childhood, not due to lapse of time, because the hadd for qadhf is not nullified by it, unlike other hudud. And it is required that the two witnesses agree on the language in which the slander occurred, by agreement. And the basis of it is His statement, the Exalted: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, lash them eighty lashes' (al-Nur: 4). (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'And proof' means in terms of proof, it is established by the testimony of two men like the hadd for drinking, and the testimony of women is not heard in it, or the slanderer confesses once. (T, Ayni) 'So if he slanders a muhsan or muhsana': as for the accused being muhsan or muhsana, it is by the text, which is His statement: 'And those who accuse...' verse. And it is required in the accused that zina be conceivable from him, meaning he is not impotent or castrated, and the woman is not closed (i.e., has no vagina). For slandering such people does not obligate the hadd. And it is required that the accused not be mute, for slandering him does not obligate the hadd, because the hadd is by request, and his request is by gesture, so it is possible that if he could speak he would confirm the slanderer. And his saying 'with zina' means that it is required that the slander be of zina. If he slanders with allusions and indirect expressions, he is not punished. For example, if a man says to a muhsan man: 'O zani!' and another says: 'You are truthful,' the speaker is punished but not the confirmer. And if he says: 'I had intercourse with so-and-so unlawfully' or 'I committed immorality with her' and the like, the hadd is not obligatory upon him, because unlawful intercourse could be from an invalid marriage. And explicit accusation of zina in any language obligates the hadd. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) 'He is punished upon his request': the condition 'upon his request' is because if he does not demand it, he is not punished, for it is his right in terms of removing disgrace. It cannot be said that the demand of the accused is not a condition, for he is punished upon the demand of one whose lineage is impugned if the accused is dead, like his son; for we say that he stands in his place, so the ruling of his demand takes the ruling of the demand of the accused. If it is said: the right of Allah predominates, so it should not require request, we say: the right of the slave, although it is overridden, it is valid for the request to be a condition as a precaution for prevention. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling from the chapter on the hadd for slander (qadhf). It begins by stating that the punishment is 80 lashes, similar to drinking, and is proven by the testimony of two men or confession. The key condition is that the accused must be muhsan (free, adult, Muslim, chaste), and the slander must be an explicit accusation of zina. If the slanderer can produce four witnesses to the zina, he avoids the hadd. The text also discusses procedural details: the judge must ask witnesses about the place and time of the slander, the witnesses must agree on the language used, and the accused must demand the punishment (if alive). It mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding how much time to give the slanderer to produce witnesses: immediately until end of session (commonly held) versus delaying to the next session (Abu Yusuf). Additionally, the passage explains that the hadd does not apply if the accused is incapable of zina (e.g., impotent, castrated, or a woman with no vagina), or if the accused is mute (since the demand could be ambiguous). The hadd is also not applied for indirect or ambiguous expressions (kinayat); only explicit words like 'O zani' suffice. The text concludes by justifying why the request of the accused is a condition: it is his right to have the matter pursued, and if he is dead, his heir (e.g., son) can demand it.

Key Terms
حد القذف (ḥadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for falsely accusing a chaste person of zina; it is 80 lashes.
محصن (muḥṣan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and chaste (i.e., has not committed zina).
كناية (kināyah): An indirect expression that does not explicitly state zina, such as 'You are immoral'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for the hadd of qadhf to be applied?
A) The slanderer must confess twice
B) The accused must be a muhsan and demand the punishment
C) Four witnesses must testify
D) The slander must be in Arabic

Key Takeaway
The hadd for slander (qadhf) is 80 lashes, but it only applies when the accused is muhsan, the accusation is explicit, and the accused demands punishment.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
6 min
The Hadd for Slander (Qadhf): Ruling, Proof, and Conditions
Defines qadhf and its equivalence to shurb punishment with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for qadhf, identify the Quranic proof, and list the conditions for the hadd to be applicable.

Core Idea
Slandering a chaste person incurs 80 lashes, but only if the victim demands it.

The hadd for qadhf is a serious punishment, but it is not automatic. The Quran prescribes eighty lashes for those who accuse chaste women without four witnesses. However, the Hanafi school elaborates that this punishment is a right of the slandered person, not a purely public penalty. In this lesson, we will examine the definition, the primary proof, the detailed conditions, and a special case where even indirect slander can incur the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, confirm what act the text discusses: qadhf (slander) meaning an explicit accusation of zina against a muhsan person. The ruling is that the slanderer receives eighty lashes, identical to the hadd for drinking alcohol.
The text equates it to shurb in both quantity and method of proof.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic verse cited: Surah al-Nur (24:4), which orders lashing those who accuse chaste women without four witnesses. Identify the imperative 'fajliduhum' as indicating obligation.
The verse is qati al-thubut and qati al-dalala in Hanafi usul.
3
List the conditions for the hadd
The text mentions several conditions: the slandered must be muhsan (free, adult, sane, Muslim, chaste); the accusation must be explicit (sarih); the slanderer must be unable to prove it with evidence; and the slandered (or his heir) must demand punishment.
If any condition fails, the hadd is not imposed.
4
Examine the special case of nafy al-nasab
Consider the ruling on saying 'You are not your father's son' in anger. The text applies istihsan, following Ibn Mas'ud, that this constitutes slander of the mother and incurs the hadd. In calm situations, it is interpreted as rebuke and no hadd.
This overrides the general qiyas that would leave it ambiguous.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Test your understanding: if a man calls his neighbor 'ya zani' but the neighbor is a known fornicator (not chaste), does the hadd apply? The answer is no, because the neighbor is not muhsan.
The condition of ihsan is crucial.

كتاب الحدود
۱۱۲
باب حد القذف
باب حد القذف
أي في بيان أحكامه
هو كحد الشرب كميّةً وثبوتاً، فلو قذف محصناً أو محصنة بزنا حد بطلبه أي
حد القذف
رجل أو امرأة أي رجلا محصنا أي امرأة محصنة أي القاذف المقذوف لأنه حقه
القذف: [وشرعاً: الرمي بالزنا وهو من الكبائر بإجماع الأمة إذا كان المقذوف محصناً وإلا فمن الصغائر. (فتح)] وهو في اللغة: الرمي مطلقا، ومنه القذافة للمقلاع، وفي القاموس التقاذف الترامي، وفي الشرع: رمي مخصوص وهو الرمي بالزنا صريحا، وهو الموجب للحد، وشرط حد القذف إحصان المقذوف، وعجز القاذف عن إثباته بالبينة، ولو قال لي بينة حاضرة في المصر أمهله القاضي إلى آخر المجلس، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يؤخره إلى المجلس الثاني. وأخر حد القذف عن حد الشرب؛ لأن جريمة الشارب متيقن بها بخلاف جريمة القاذف، فإن القذف خبر محتمل للصدق والكذب والمناسبة بينهما أن حد القذف مثل حد الشرب. (عيني، معدن)
هو
عن
كحد الشرب: أي حد القذف مثل حد الشرب في كونه ثمانين جلدة، وفي كونه ثابتاً بشهادة رجلين، ويسألهما القاضي عن القذف ما هو؟ وكيف هو؟ فإن قالا نشهد أنه قال له يا زاني، قبلت شهادتهما، وحد القاذف إن كانا عدلين وينبغي أن يسألهما . المكان؛ لاحتمال أن يكون قذفه في دار الحرب، أو دار البغي، وعن الزمان؛ لاحتمال أن يكون قذفه في صباه لا لاحتمال التقادم؛ لأن حد القذف لا يبطل به، بخلاف سائر الحدود، ويشترط اتفاق الشاهدين على اللغة التي وقع القذف بها بالاتفاق، والأصل فيه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً (النور:٤) (مستخلص، فتح) وثبوتاً: أي من
بصريح
الثبوت يثبت بشهادة رجلين كحد الشرب ولا تسمع فيه شهادة النساء أو يقر القاذف مرة. (ط، عيني) فلو قذف محصناً أو محصنة: أما كون المقذوف محصناً أو محصنة، فبالنص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ ﴾ الآية، ويشترط في المقذوف تصور الزنا منه بأن لا يكون محبوباً أو عنيناً أو خصياً، ولا تكون المرأة رتقا، فإن القذف فيهم لا يوجب الحد، ويشترط أن لا يكون المقذوف أخرس، فإن قذفه لا يوجب الحد؛ لأن الحد بالطلب، وطلبه بالإشارة فيحتمل أنه لو كان ينطق لصدق القاذف، وقوله: "بزنا" أي يشترط أن يكون القذف الزنا، فلو قذفه بالكنايات والتعريض لا يحد بأن قال رجل للرجل المحصن: "يا زاني"، وقال آخر: "صدقت" يحد القائل دون المصدق، ولو قال: جامعت فلانة حراماً أو فجرت بها ونحوهما لا يجب عليه الحد؛ لأن الجماع الحرام قد يكون بنكاح فاسد، وصريح الزنا من أي لسان كان يوجب الحد. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) حد بطلبه : قيد "بطلبه" لأنه لو لم يطالبه لا يحد؛ لأن فيه حقه من حيث دفع العار، لا يقال: مطالبة المقذوف ليس بشرط، فإنه يحد بمطالبة من يقع القدح في نسبه إذا كان المقذوف ميتاً كابنه؛ لأنا نقول: إنه قائم مقامه، فأخذ حكم مطالبته حكم مطالبة المقذوف فإن قيل: حق ا الله غالب فكان ينبغي أن لا يشترط الطلب، قلنا: حق العبد وإن كان مغلوباً فيه، لكنه يصلح أن يكون المطالبة شرطاً احتيالاً للدراً. (مستخلص، فتح)

كتاب الحدود
۱۱۳
باب حد القذف
متفرقاً، ولا ينزع عنه غير الفرو والحشو، وإحصانه بكونه مكلفاً حراً مسلماً
وهو الذي يلبس من الجلد
المقذوف
عفيفا فلا يحد بقذف العبد فلا يحد بقذف الكافر
عن الزنا، فلو قال لغيره : لست لأبيك أو لست بابن فلان في غضب حد، وفي غيره لا
أي رجل
أي في حالة غضب ومشاجرة
متفرقاً: أي ضرباً متفرقاً على أعضاء القاذف أي يفرق الضرب على أعضائه كما في حد الزنا والشرب؛ لئلا يودي إلى التلف. (مستخلص فتح ولا ينزع عنه: أي لا يجرد القاذف عن ثيابه للتخفيف به؛ لأن سببه غير مقطوع به لاحتمال صدقه وإن كان القاذف عاجزاً عن إثبات الزنا إلا أن الفرو والحشو يمنعان عن وصول الألم به فلا يحصل المقصود فينزعان بخلاف حد الزنا والشرب؛ لأن سببهما متيقن به رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۳/۱] (مستخلص) وإحصانه: [ أي إحصان المقذوف يثبت بشهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين وبعلم القاضي، ويشترط وجوده وقت الحد. (عيني، فتح)] أي شرائط الإحصان في المقذوف خمسة، فإذا فقد واحد منها لا يكون محصناً، الأول: كون المقذوف مكلفاً أي عاقلاً بالغاً، وإنما شرط هذا؛ لأن العار لا يلحق الصبي والمجنون، والثاني: الحرية؛ لأن اسم الإحصان يطلق عليه، قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَاتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ (النساء: ٢٥) وهي الحرائر، ويثبت الحرية بإقرار القاذف، أو بالبينة إذا أنكر، والثالث: الإسلام؛ لقوله علي : " من أشرك بالله فليس محصن"، الرابع: العفّة؛ لأن غير العفيف لا يلحقه العار، ولأن القاذف صادق في قذفه فلا يستحق العقوبة، ولما كان الشرط الأول متضمناً لشرطين، فصارت الشروط خمسة. عفيفاً: بأن لم يكن زنى بامرأة ولا وطء بشبهة ولا بنكاح فاسد في عمره. (فتح) عن الزنا: احترازاً عن الوطء الحرام في الملك كوطء زوجته في حيضها، أو وطء أمته المجوسية، فإنه لا يخرج الواطي عن أن يكون محصناً، ولو وطء الحرام في غير الملك كالوطء بشبهة أو بنكاح فاسد، أو وطء الجارية المشتركة، ووطء من هي محرمة عليه على التأبيد يخرجه عن الإحصان. (مستخلص، فتح)
في غضب :حد [ أي القائل إذا كانت أمه محصنة؛ لأنه قذف لأمه حقيقة. (عيني)] أي من قال لغيره: لست لأبيك أو لست بابن فلان لأبيه الذي يعرف له، فإن كان هذا القول : حالة الغضب حد القائل إذا كانت أمه حرة مسلمة؛ لأنه إذا كان من غير أبيه المنسوب إليه كان من الزنا ضرورة، واشترط حالة الغضب؛ لأنه في غير حالة الغضب قد يراد به المعاتبة أي أنت لا تشبه أباك في المروءة والسخاء، فلا يحد مع الاحتمال، وفي حالة الغضب يراد به الحقيقة وكذا إذا قال: إنك ابن فلان لغير أبيه يحد إذا كان في حالة المشاتمة، وفي حالة الرضا لا يحد، والقياس أن لا يكون قذفا في الأحوال كلها للاحتمال وجه الاستحسان ما روي عن ابن مسعود له قال: لا حد إلا في قذف محصنة أو نفي رجل من أبيه، ولو نفاه عن أمه بأن قال: لست لأمك لا يجب عليه الحد؛ لأنه صدق؛ لأن النسب إلى الآباء فقط. رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۳/۱] (فتح، مستخلص)
لا: أي في حالة غير غضب لا يحد. (عيني)
Book of Hudud. Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf: meaning in explanation of its rulings. It is like the hadd of drinking (shurb) in quantity and establishment. So if one slanders a muhsan male or muhsana female with zina, he is punished upon their request. 'Hadd al-Qadhf' is a man or woman, meaning a muhsan man or a muhsana woman, meaning the slanderer and the slandered, because it is his right. 'Qadhf' legally: accusing of zina, and it is among the major sins by consensus of the ummah if the slandered is muhsan, otherwise it is among minor sins. (Fath) Linguistically: throwing absolutely, from which comes al-qadhafah for a sling. In al-Qamus: al-taqadhuf is mutual throwing. Legally: a specific accusation, which is explicit accusation of zina, and it is what necessitates the hadd. The condition for hadd al-qadhf is the ihsan of the slandered, and the inability of the slanderer to prove it with evidence. If he says 'I have evidence present in the city', the judge gives him time until the end of the session. According to Abu Yusuf, he postpones him to the second session. The hadd of qadhf is delayed after the hadd of shurb because the crime of the drinker is certain, unlike the crime of the slanderer, for the slander is a report that may be true or false. The suitability between them is that the hadd of qadhf is like the hadd of shurb. (Ayni, Ma'din) 'Like the hadd of shurb': meaning the hadd of qadhf is like the hadd of shurb in being eighty lashes, and in being established by the testimony of two men. The judge asks them about the slander: what is it? How is it? If they say 'We testify that he said to him 'O zani',' their testimony is accepted, and the slanderer is punished if they are just ('adl). He should ask them about the place, because it is possible that the slander occurred in dar al-harb or dar al-baghi; and about the time, because it is possible that the slander occurred in his childhood; not because of prescription, because the hadd of qadhf is not invalidated by it, unlike other hudud. It is required that the two witnesses agree on the language in which the slander occurred by consensus. The basis for it is the saying of Allah: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses - lash them eighty lashes.' (al-Nur:4) (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'And establishment': meaning from the perspective of proof, it is established by the testimony of two men like the hadd of shurb, and the testimony of women is not heard in it, or the slanderer confesses once. (T, Ayni) 'So if one slanders a muhsan male or muhsana female': As for the slandered being muhsan or muhsana, that is by the text, which is His saying 'And those who accuse...' etc. It is required in the slandered that zina be conceivable from him, i.e., he is not impotent, or a eunuch, or castrated, and the woman is not obstructed (ratqa). For slandering such persons does not necessitate the hadd. It is required that the slandered not be mute, for slandering him does not necessitate the hadd because the hadd is by request, and his request is by gesture, so it is possible that if he could speak, he would confirm the slanderer. And his saying 'with zina' means it is required that the slander be of zina. If he slanders with kinayah (allusions) and ta'rid (indirect speech), he is not punished. For example, a man says to a muhsan man 'O zani,' and another says 'You have spoken the truth' - the speaker is punished, not the one who confirms. If he says 'I had illicit intercourse with so-and-so unlawfully' or 'I committed fujur with her' and similar, the hadd is not obligatory upon him because unlawful intercourse may be through a fasid marriage. Explicit zina in any language necessitates the hadd. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) 'He is punished upon his request': The restriction 'upon his request' is because if he does not demand it, he is not punished, for it is his right in terms of removing disgrace. It cannot be said that the demand of the slandered is not a condition, for he is punished at the request of one whose lineage is impugned if the slandered is dead, like his son; because we say he stands in his place, so his request takes the ruling of the slandered's request. If it is said that the right of Allah predominates, so it would be appropriate not to require the request; we say: the right of the slave, although it is overridden, is still suitable to be made a condition to facilitate [the punishment]. (Mustakhlas, Fath) [Page 114] Book of Hudud. 113. Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. 'Distributed' and he is not stripped except of the fur and the padding. And his ihsan: being mukallaf, free, Muslim, chaste. So the slave is not punished for slandering a slave. So the disbeliever is not punished for slandering a disbeliever. 'From zina' is to exclude unlawful intercourse within ownership like intercourse with his wife during her menses, or with his Magian slave-girl, for that does not remove the person from being muhsan. But unlawful intercourse outside ownership like intercourse with shubha or fasid marriage, or intercourse with a jointly owned slave-girl, or with one who is permanently forbidden to him, removes him from ihsan. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'In anger': hadd [meaning the speaker, if his mother is muhsana, because he slandered his mother in reality. (Ayni)] That is, whoever says to another 'You are not your father's son' or 'You are not the son of so-and-so' to his known father, if this statement is in a state of anger, the speaker is punished if his mother is free and Muslim, because if he is not from his ascribed father, then he is necessarily from zina. The condition of anger is because when not in anger, it may be intended as rebuke, meaning 'you do not resemble your father in manliness and generosity', so he is not punished due to probability. In a state of anger, the literal meaning is intended. Similarly, if he says 'You are the son of so-and-so' to someone other than his father, he is punished if in a state of quarrel. In a state of contentment, he is not punished. The analogy would be that it is not slander in all cases due to probability. The basis of istihsan is what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'There is no hadd except for slandering a muhsana or denying a man's paternity of his father.' If he denies him of his mother by saying 'You are not your mother's son', the hadd is not obligatory upon him because it is true, for lineage is only through fathers. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'No': meaning in a state other than anger, he is not punished. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the punishment for slander (qadhf) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that the hadd for qadhf is exactly like that for drinking alcohol (shurb) in two respects: quantity (eighty lashes) and method of proof (requires two male witnesses or confession). The primary evidence is Quran 24:4. Several conditions are detailed: the slandered must be muhsan (chaste, free, adult, sane, Muslim), the slander must be explicit (sarih) accusations of zina, and the slanderer must be unable to prove his claim. The slanderer's victim (or his heir if deceased) must demand punishment; it is not enforced automatically. The passage then discusses the execution of the lashing: it must be distributed over the body, not concentrated, to avoid death. The slanderer is not stripped of his clothes except for fur and padding that would reduce pain, because the cause (the slander) is not certain (it could be true). The five conditions of ihsan for the slandered are enumerated: mukallaf (accountable), free, Muslim, chaste, and never having committed zina or any illegal intercourse (including shubha or fasid marriage). The passage concludes with a special ruling: saying 'You are not your father's son' in anger constitutes slander and incurs the hadd, because it necessarily implies zina of the mother. However, if said calmly, it is interpreted as rebuke and no hadd. This is based on istihsan from the athar of Ibn Mas'ud, overriding the qiyas that would consider it ambiguous in all cases. The Hanafi position is clear: the punishment is a right of the individual, so it requires their demand; the judge does not initiate it.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Legally: explicit accusation of zina against a muhsan person, which necessitates the hadd of eighty lashes.
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste (has never committed zina or illegal intercourse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the punishment for slandering a muhsan person if the slanderer cannot prove the accusation?
A) 40 lashes
B) 80 lashes
C) 100 lashes
D) Death by stoning

Key Takeaway
The hadd for qadhf is a fixed punishment of 80 lashes, conditioned on the victim's demand and the slanderer's inability to prove the accusation.

Conditions of Ihsan for the Slandered (Qadhf)
Lists the five conditions for a person to be considered muhsan in qadhf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan required for the slandered to be eligible for hadd al-qadhf, and identify which acts of intercourse break the condition of chastity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ihsan in qadhf has five conditions; losing chastity via any unlawful intercourse outside ownership nullifies it.

The hadd penalty for false slander (qadhf) only applies when the victim is legally 'muhsan' — protected by the law. This status is defined by five conditions. In this lesson, we unpack each condition and clarify what does and does not break the all-important condition of chastity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal institution
Recognize that the passage defines 'ihsan' as a prerequisite for the hadd of qadhf. The slandered must be muhsan for the penalty to apply.
2
List the five conditions
Extract the five conditions: (1) mukallaf (sane, adult), (2) free, (3) Muslim, (4) chaste, and (5) not having committed unlawful intercourse (note: the first condition includes two sub-conditions).
Freedom is a distinct condition; the Hanafi school uniquely requires it.
3
Analyze the fourth condition: chastity
Understand what breaks chastity: any zina, intercourse with shubha, or fasid marriage. But intercourse within ownership (e.g., with wife during menses, Magian slave-girl) does not break it.
The key distinction is between 'unlawful intercourse outside ownership' vs. 'within ownership'.
4
Examine the proofs
Note that freedom is proven by Quran 4:25 (al-muhsanat = free women) and Islam by a hadith of 'Ali. The other conditions are based on preventing disgrace and the slanderer's truthfulness.
5
Review practical tests
Apply: if a man slanders a woman who once had intercourse with a jointly-owned slave-girl, she is not muhsan because that act breaks chastity. If he slanders a woman who had intercourse with her husband during menses, she remains muhsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإحصانه: [ أي إحصان المقذوف يثبت بشهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين وبعلم القاضي، ويشترط وجوده وقت الحد. (عيني، فتح)] أي شرائط الإحصان في المقذوف خمسة، فإذا فقد واحد منها لا يكون محصناً، الأول: كون المقذوف مكلفاً أي عاقلاً بالغاً، وإنما شرط هذا؛ لأن العار لا يلحق الصبي والمجنون، والثاني: الحرية؛ لأن اسم الإحصان يطلق عليه، قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَاتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ (النساء: ٢٥) وهي الحرائر، ويثبت الحرية بإقرار القاذف، أو بالبينة إذا أنكر، والثالث: الإسلام؛ لقوله علي : " من أشرك بالله فليس محصن"، الرابع: العفّة؛ لأن غير العفيف لا يلحقه العار، ولأن القاذف صادق في قذفه فلا يستحق العقوبة، ولما كان الشرط الأول متضمناً لشرطين، فصارت الشروط خمسة. عفيفاً: بأن لم يكن زنى بامرأة ولا وطء بشبهة ولا بنكاح فاسد في عمره. (فتح) عن الزنا: احترازاً عن الوطء الحرام في الملك كوطء زوجته في حيضها، أو وطء أمته المجوسية، فإنه لا يخرج الواطي عن أن يكون محصناً، ولو وطء الحرام في غير الملك كالوطء بشبهة أو بنكاح فاسد، أو وطء الجارية المشتركة، ووطء من هي محرمة عليه على التأبيد يخرجه عن الإحصان. (مستخلص، فتح)
And his ihsan: [i.e., the ihsan of the slandered is established by the testimony of two men or a man and two women, and by the knowledge of the judge, and its existence is required at the time of the hadd. (Ayni, Fath)] Meaning the conditions of ihsan in the slandered are five. If any one is absent, he is not muhsan. First: the slandered being mukallaf, i.e., sane and adult. This is required because disgrace does not befall the child or the insane. Second: freedom, because the term ihsan is applied to it. Allah said: 'Then upon them half the punishment of the muhsanat (free women) from the punishment.' (al-Nisa:25) and they are free women. Freedom is established by the slanderer's acknowledgment or by evidence if he denies. Third: Islam, because 'Ali said: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' Fourth: chastity, because the unchaste does not suffer disgrace, and because the slanderer is truthful in his slander so he does not deserve punishment. Since the first condition includes two conditions, the total becomes five. 'Chaste': meaning he has not committed zina with a woman, nor intercourse with shubha, nor through a fasid marriage in his lifetime. (Fath) 'From zina' is to exclude unlawful intercourse within ownership like intercourse with his wife during her menses or with his Magian slave-girl, for that does not remove the person from being muhsan. But unlawful intercourse outside ownership like intercourse with shubha or a fasid marriage, or intercourse with a jointly owned slave-girl, or with one who is permanently forbidden to him, removes him from ihsan. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This is a definition ruling explaining the five conditions of ihsan (the legal status that makes a person eligible to be the victim of hadd al-qadhf and receive the protection of the law). The conditions are: (1) being mukallaf (sane and adult) because children and the insane do not feel disgrace; (2) being free, derived from Quran 4:25 where 'muhsanat' refers to free women; (3) being Muslim, based on a hadith from 'Ali; (4) being chaste, meaning the person has never committed zina or any form of illegal intercourse (including intercourse through shubha or fasid marriage). However, unlawful intercourse within ownership (e.g., with one's wife during menses or with a Magian slave-girl) does not break ihsan. The passage also notes that the slandered must be chaste at the time of hadd; if he lost chastity after the slander but before the hadd, the hadd is not applied. The Hanafi school is distinctive in requiring freedom as a condition; other schools may not. The text also clarifies that the slandered can prove his ihsan by two male witnesses or a man and two women, or by the judge's knowledge. The slanderer's acknowledgment of the slandered's freedom is also accepted.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): A legal status consisting of five conditions: mukallaf, free, Muslim, chaste, and never having committed illegal intercourse.
رتق (ratq): A woman with an obstruction in the vagina, making intercourse impossible; slandering such a woman does not incur hadd because zina is not conceivable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the slandered to be muhsan?
A) Being adult and sane
B) Being male
C) Being Muslim
D) Being free

Key Takeaway
A slandered person must satisfy five conditions of ihsan; any unlawful intercourse outside ownership breaks chastity and removes ihsan.

Slander by Paternity Denial in Anger (Hadd al-Qadhf)
Ruling with proof on paternity denial slander

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity denial slander and apply the distinction between anger and calmness to determine whether hadd is imposed.

Core Idea
Paternity denial in anger is slander (qadhf) and incurs hadd; calm denial is ambiguous and not punished.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a nuanced form of slander: denying someone's paternity. The Hanafi school distinguishes sharply based on the speaker's emotional state. In anger, the literal meaning (imputing zina to the mother) is intended, so the hadd punishment applies if the mother is muhsana. In calmness, the statement is likely a rebuke ('you don't resemble your father') and no hadd is imposed. The ruling also extends to attributing a person to a false father. The text demonstrates the interplay of qiyas and istihsan, with the athar of Ibn Mas'ud serving as the decisive evidence for the exceptional rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the key condition
The act is a verbal statement: 'You are not your father's son' or similar paternity denial. The key condition is whether it is said in anger or calmly. Identify this distinction in the text.
2
State the ruling for each context
In anger: the speaker incurs hadd (if mother is muhsana). In calm: no hadd. Also note the ruling for saying 'you are the son of so-and-so' to someone other than the father.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogy) reasoning
By pure analogy, such statements in any context would not be slander because they are ambiguous (could be rebuke). This is the default ruling.
Qiyas would yield: no hadd in all cases.
4
Follow the istihsan (juristic preference) reasoning
The athar of Ibn Mas'ud overrides qiyas: 'لا حد إلا في قذف محصنة أو نفي رجل من أبيه' – this specifically includes paternity denial. In anger, the ambiguity is removed, so hadd applies. This is the basis of istihsan.
Istihsan is a source of law in the Hanafi school, giving weight to a specific evidence over general analogy.
5
Apply the ruling to related cases
Consider denial from mother's side: 'You are not your mother's son' – no hadd because lineage is only through the father, so it is literally true. Also note that the mother must be muhsana (free, Muslim, chaste) for the hadd to apply.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في غضب :حد [ أي القائل إذا كانت أمه محصنة؛ لأنه قذف لأمه حقيقة. (عيني)] أي من قال لغيره: لست لأبيك أو لست بابن فلان لأبيه الذي يعرف له، فإن كان هذا القول : حالة الغضب حد القائل إذا كانت أمه حرة مسلمة؛ لأنه إذا كان من غير أبيه المنسوب إليه كان من الزنا ضرورة، واشترط حالة الغضب؛ لأنه في غير حالة الغضب قد يراد به المعاتبة أي أنت لا تشبه أباك في المروءة والسخاء، فلا يحد مع الاحتمال، وفي حالة الغضب يراد به الحقيقة وكذا إذا قال: إنك ابن فلان لغير أبيه يحد إذا كان في حالة المشاتمة، وفي حالة الرضا لا يحد، والقياس أن لا يكون قذفا في الأحوال كلها للاحتمال وجه الاستحسان ما روي عن ابن مسعود له قال: لا حد إلا في قذف محصنة أو نفي رجل من أبيه، ولو نفاه عن أمه بأن قال: لست لأمك لا يجب عليه الحد؛ لأنه صدق؛ لأن النسب إلى الآباء فقط. رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۳/۱] (فتح، مستخلص)
لا: أي في حالة غير غضب لا يحد. (عيني)
In anger: hadd [meaning the speaker, if his mother is muhsana, because he slanders his mother in reality. (Ayni)] That is, whoever says to another 'You are not your father's son' or 'You are not the son of so-and-so' to his known father, if this statement is in a state of anger, the speaker is punished if his mother is free and Muslim, because if he is not from his ascribed father, then he is necessarily from zina. The condition of anger is because when not in anger, it may be intended as rebuke, meaning 'you do not resemble your father in manliness and generosity', so he is not punished due to probability. In a state of anger, the literal meaning is intended. Similarly, if he says 'You are the son of so-and-so' to someone other than his father, he is punished if in a state of quarrel. In a state of contentment, he is not punished. The analogy would be that it is not slander in all cases due to probability. The basis of istihsan is what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'There is no hadd except for slandering a muhsana or denying a man's paternity of his father.' If he denies him of his mother by saying 'You are not your mother's son', the hadd is not obligatory upon him because it is true, for lineage is only through fathers. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'No': meaning in a state other than anger, he is not punished. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This is a ruling on a specific form of slander: denying a person's paternity. The Hanafi school distinguishes between two contexts: if the statement is made in anger, it is taken literally and constitutes slander (qadhf) because it implies that the mother committed zina, provided the mother is muhsana (free and Muslim). If the statement is made calmly, it is interpreted as a metaphorical rebuke (e.g., 'you do not resemble your father in good qualities'), so no hadd is imposed. The qiyas (analogy) would suggest that such statements are ambiguous and should never incur hadd, but istihsan (juristic preference) based on the athar of Ibn Mas'ud overturns this: the hadd applies specifically to denial of paternity from the father's side in anger. Denial from the mother's side (e.g., 'you are not your mother's son') never incurs hadd because lineage is through the father. The ruling also applies to saying 'you are the son of so-and-so' to attribute someone to a person other than his father, which is essentially the same as denial. The Hanafi position is thus nuanced, considering intention (indicated by anger) and the specific words used.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to a stronger evidence (here the athar of Ibn Mas'ud) to impose hadd for paternity denial in anger.
نفي (nafy): Denial of paternity; in this context, saying 'you are not your father's son' which implies zina of the mother.
محصنة (muhsana): A free, Muslim woman who has not been convicted of zina; slandering such a person incurs the hadd of qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man calmly says to another 'You are not your father's son,' is he subject to hadd al-qadhf?
A) Yes, because it is slander
B) No, because it is likely meant as rebuke
C) Yes, but only if the mother is Muslim
D) No, because paternity denial is never punishable

Key Takeaway
Paternity denial slander incurs hadd only when said in anger and when the mother is muhsana; calm statements are not punishable, nor is denial from the mother's side.

Conditions for Ihsan in Hadd al-Qadhf and Method of Punishment
Ruling on administration of lashes and accused's qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan for the accused in hadd al-qadhf and explain why each condition is necessary for the hadd penalty to apply.

Core Idea
In qadhf, the penalty applies only if the accused is muhsan: free, adult, Muslim, and chaste from zina.

The hadd punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf) is 80 lashes, but this penalty is only triggered if the accused qualifies as muhsan (protected). In this lesson, we will examine the precise conditions that define ihsan in the Hanafi school, as outlined in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. Understanding these conditions is essential because if any one is missing, the slanderer escapes the hadd penalty, though a ta'zir may apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with hadd al-qadhf: 80 lashes administered distributively. Determine the hukm level: wajib (hadd is wajib upon proof).
2
List the conditions for ihsan
Extract the five conditions: mukallaf (adult and sane), free, Muslim, chaste from zina. Note that the text lists four but mukallaf includes two, making five.
3
Understand each condition's rationale
Grasp why each condition is required: shame does not attach to a child/madman; ihsan linguistically implies freedom; Islam elevates status; chastity ensures the slanderer is lying.
4
Apply the conditions to examples
Test scenarios: a slave, a disbeliever, a child, or a person with a history of zina are not muhsan. Hence, no hadd for the slanderer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود
باب حد القذف
متفرقاً، ولا ينزع عنه غير الفرو والحشو، وإحصانه بكونه مكلفاً حراً مسلماً عفيفاً عن الزنا، فلا يحد بقذف العبد ولا بقذف الكافر.
وإحصانه: [ أي إحصان المقذوف يثبت بشهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين وبعلم القاضي، ويشترط وجوده وقت الحد. (عيني، فتح)] أي شرائط الإحصان في المقذوف خمسة، فإذا فقد واحد منها لا يكون محصناً، الأول: كون المقذوف مكلفاً أي عاقلاً بالغاً، وإنما شرط هذا؛ لأن العار لا يلحق الصبي والمجنون، والثاني: الحرية؛ لأن اسم الإحصان يطلق عليه، قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَاتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ﴾ (النساء: ٢٥) وهي الحرائر، ويثبت الحرية بإقرار القاذف، أو بالبينة إذا أنكر، والثالث: الإسلام؛ لقوله علي : " من أشرك بالله فليس محصن"، الرابع: العفّة؛ لأن غير العفيف لا يلحقه العار، ولأن القاذف صادق في قذفه فلا يستحق العقوبة، ولما كان الشرط الأول متضمناً لشرطين، فصارت الشروط خمسة. عفيفاً: بأن لم يكن زنى بامرأة ولا وطء بشبهة ولا بنكاح فاسد في عمره. (فتح) عن الزنا: احترازاً عن الوطء الحرام في الملك كوطء زوجته في حيضها، أو وطء أمته المجوسية، فإنه لا يخرج الواطي عن أن يكون محصناً، ولو وطء الحرام في غير الملك كالوطء بشبهة أو بنكاح فاسد، أو وطء الجارية المشتركة، ووطء من هي محرمة عليه على التأبيد يخرجه عن الإحصان. (مستخلص، فتح)
The Book of Hadd. Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. (Lashes) distributed, and he is not stripped except the fur and the padding. His ihsan (the accused's requalification) is that he be: accountable, free, Muslim, chaste from zina. So he is not subject to hadd for slandering a slave, nor for slandering a disbeliever. His ihsan: (the ihsan of the accused is established by testimony of two men or a man and two women and by the judge's knowledge, and its presence is required at the time of hadd.) That is, the conditions of ihsan in the accused are five: if one is missing he is not muhsan. First: the accused being mukallaf, i.e., sane and adult; this is required because shame does not affect a child or madman. Second: freedom; because the name ihsan is applied to it, Allah said: "then upon them half the punishment of the muhsanat" (4:25), meaning free women; freedom is established by the slanderer's confession or by evidence if he denies. Third: Islam; because of the saying of 'Ali: "Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan." Fourth: chastity; because shame does not affect one who is not chaste, and because the slanderer is truthful in his slander so he does not deserve punishment. Since the first condition includes two conditions, the conditions become five. Chaste: meaning he has never committed zina with a woman, nor intercourse with shubha, nor invalid marriage in his life. (Fath) [Chaste] from zina: as a precaution against unlawful intercourse in ownership like intercourse with his wife during her menstruation, or intercourse with his Magian female slave; for this does not exit the one who does it from being muhsan. As for unlawful intercourse not in ownership like intercourse by shubha or invalid marriage, or intercourse with a jointly-owned slave girl, or intercourse with one who is eternally forbidden to him, it removes him from ihsan. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the chapter of hadd al-qadhf. The passage first states the manner of punishment: the slanderer is given 80 lashes that are distributed over different parts of the body (not concentrated in one area) to avoid causing death. He is not stripped of clothes except the outer garments (fur) and the padding (hashw) that would lessen the pain. This is because the cause of the punishment is not certain (there is a possibility the slanderer is truthful). The accused (al-maqdhuf) must satisfy five conditions to be muhsan: (1) being accountable (mukallaf, i.e., adult and sane), because shame does not attach to a child or madman; (2) free, because the term 'ihsan' in the Qur'an refers to free women; (3) Muslim, as per 'Ali's statement; (4) chaste (afif) from zina, meaning he never committed illegal sexual intercourse, including intercourse with shubha or invalid marriage; (5) chastity from zina includes not committing zina even in cases like intercourse with a slave he co-owns or with a woman permanently forbidden. The text adds that if the accused is a slave or a disbeliever, the hadd is not applied to the slanderer. The commentary clarifies the proofs for each condition: the Qur'anic verse for freedom, and athar for Islam. The conditions are presented as five, though the text lists four because the first (mukallaf) actually includes two conditions (adult and sane).

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): In the context of qadhf, the status of the accused being a free adult Muslim who has never committed zina, making the slanderer liable for hadd.
مُتفرقاً (mutafarriqan): The lashes are to be distributed across the slanderer's body, not all on one spot, to avoid causing death.
حشو (hashw): Padding or underclothes that would reduce the pain of lashes; these must be removed before punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the accused to be muhsan in hadd al-qadhf?
A) Being free
B) Being Muslim
C) Being married
D) Being chaste from zina

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf is only established when the accused meets five conditions: being mukallaf, free, Muslim, and chaste from zina—without any one, the slanderer is not liable for hadd.
